Translation Evaluation Packet

Language: Chinese (Simplified)

Reviewer: Chinese (Simplified) Reviewer

Total Items: 48

Date Generated: 2025-11-30

Instructions for Reviewers

Thank you for participating in this translation quality evaluation. Please follow these guidelines:

  1. Read carefully: Review the original English text, the translation, and the back-translation.
  2. Rate each criterion: Use the 1-5 scale for each quality dimension.
  3. Note critical errors: Flag any translation errors that could harm patients.
  4. Be objective: Evaluate based on accuracy, not personal preference.

Rating Scale

  • 5 - Excellent: Perfect or near-perfect quality
  • 4 - Good: Minor issues that don't affect meaning
  • 3 - Acceptable: Some issues but core meaning preserved
  • 2 - Poor: Significant issues affecting comprehension
  • 1 - Very Poor: Major errors or incomprehensible
SAFETY CRITICAL: If you find any translation that could lead to patient harm (wrong medication instructions, missing warnings, etc.), please mark it as a critical error and describe the issue in the notes section.

Evaluation Criteria Reference

CriterionDescription
Overall AccuracyHow accurately does the translation convey the original meaning?
Medical AccuracyAre medical terms and concepts translated correctly?
Cultural AppropriatenessIs the translation culturally appropriate for the target audience?
ClarityHow easy is the translation to understand for a native speaker?
Safety PreservationAre all warnings.and safety information preserved?
ActionabilityCan a patient follow the instructions based on this translation?

Evaluation Items

Item: EVAL_0004 | Document: CARD_001 | Model: Model C

Original English:

Heart Failure - Discharge Heart failure is a condition in which the heart is no longer able to pump oxygen-rich blood to the rest of the body efficiently. When symptoms become severe, a hospital stay may be necessary. This article discusses what you need to do to take care of yourself when you leave the hospital. When You're in the Hospital You were in the hospital to have your heart failure treated. Heart failure occurs when the muscles of your heart are weak or have trouble relaxing, or both. Your heart is a pump that moves fluids through your body. As with any pump, if the flow out of the pump is not enough, fluids do not move well and they get stuck in places they should not be. In your body, this means that fluid collects in your lungs, abdomen, and legs. While you were in the hospital: Your health care team closely adjusted the fluids you drank or received through an intravenous (IV) line. They also watched and measured how much urine you produced. You may have received medicines to help your body get rid of extra fluids. You may have had tests to check how well your heart was working. What to Expect at Home Your energy will slowly return. You may need help taking care of yourself when you first get home. You may feel sad or depressed. All of these things are normal. Checking Yourself at Home Weigh yourself every morning on the same scale when you get up -- before you eat but after you use the bathroom. Make sure you are wearing similar clothing each time you weigh yourself. Write down your weight every day on a chart so that you can keep track of it. Throughout the day, ask yourself: Is my energy level normal? Do I get more short of breath when I am doing my everyday activities? Are my clothes or shoes feeling tight? Are my ankles or legs swelling? Am I coughing more often? Does my cough sound wet? Do I get short of breath at night or when I lie down? If you are having new (or different) symptoms, ask yourself: Did I eat something different than usua...

Translation (Chinese (Simplified)):

心力衰竭 - 出院指导 心力衰竭是一种疾病，指心脏不能再有效地把含氧血液泵送到全身。当症状变得严重时，可能需要住院治疗。本文将介绍出院后你需要做些什么来照顾自己。 在医院期间 你这次住院是为了治疗心力衰竭。心力衰竭是指心脏肌肉变弱，或放松困难，或两者都有问题。 你的心脏就像一个泵，把体内的液体输送到全身。和任何泵一样，如果泵出来的流量不够，液体就不能很好地流动，会停留在不该停留的地方。在你的身体里，这意味着液体会积聚在肺部、腹部和腿部。 在你住院期间： 你的医疗团队会严格调节你喝的液体量或通过静脉输液（IV）进入体内的液体量。他们还会观察并测量你排出的尿量。 你可能会使用帮助身体排出多余液体的药物。 你可能会做一些检查，以了解心脏的工作情况。 回家后会有什么情况 你的体力会慢慢恢复。刚回家时，你可能需要别人帮忙照顾自己。你可能会感到伤心或情绪低落。这些都是正常的。 在家自我检查 每天早晨起床后，用同一台体重秤称体重——在吃东西前、上完厕所后称。每次称重时，尽量穿相似的衣服。把每天的体重记录在表格上，方便自己随时查看变化。 在一天中，问问自己： 我的精力水平正常吗？ 做日常活动时，我会不会更容易气短？ 我的衣服或鞋子有没有变紧？ 我的脚踝或腿有没有肿胀？ 我是不是更常咳嗽？咳嗽时声音是不是有痰、很湿？ 我晚上或躺下时会不会气短？ 如果你出现新的（或不同的）症状，问问自己： 我是不是吃了和平时不一样的东西，或者尝试了新食物？ 我是不是按时、按正确的方法服用了所有药物？ 饮食和饮水 你的医疗服务提供者可能会要求你限制饮水量。 当你的心力衰竭不太严重时，可能不需要严格限制饮水。 当心力衰竭加重时，可能会要求你每天把饮水量限制在 6 到 9 杯（1.5 到 2 升）。 你需要少吃盐。盐会让你更口渴，而口渴会让你喝太多水。额外的盐也会让液体更容易滞留在体内。很多尝起来不咸、或者你没有额外加盐的食物，其实仍然含有很多盐。 你可能需要服用利尿剂，也叫“水丸”。 不要喝酒。酒精会让心肌工作得更吃力。在有特殊场合、可能会提供酒精饮料和你需要避免的食物时，先问问你的医疗服务提供者该怎么办。 如果你吸烟，请戒烟。如果需要，向他人寻求戒烟帮助。不要让任何人在你家里吸烟。 进一步了解哪些食物有助于让你的心脏和血管更健康。 避免高脂肪食物。 尽量不要去快餐店吃饭。 避免一些预制食品和冷冻食品。 尽量远离让你感到压力大的事情。如果你总是感到压力很大，或者非常伤心，请和你的医疗服务提供者沟通，他们可以转介你去看心理咨询师。 按时服用心脏药物 在出院前，把所有处方药都配好。非常重要的一点是，你必须严格按照医疗服务提供者的嘱咐服药。未经医疗服务提供者同意，不要擅自服用其他药物或草药。 用水送服药物。不要用葡萄柚汁送服，因为葡萄柚汁可能会改变身体对某些药物的吸收。问问你的医疗服务提供者或药师，这对你是否会造成问题。 下面这些药物常用于治疗心力衰竭的患者。但有时出于某些原因，这些药物可能对你不安全。这些药物可能有助于保护你的心脏。如果你还没有使用这些药物，请和你的医疗服务提供者讨论： 抗血小板药物（blood thinners，血液稀释剂），如阿司匹林或氯吡格雷（Plavix），帮助防止血液凝固 抗凝药物（blood thinners，血液稀释剂），如华法林（Coumadin），帮助防止血液凝固 β 受体阻滞剂（beta blocker）和 ACE 抑制剂（ACE inhibitor），以及其他用于降低血压和治疗心肌的药物 他汀类药物（statins）或其他降胆固醇药物 在改变用药方式前，一定要先咨询你的医疗服务提供者。绝对不要自行停用这些心脏药物，或你正在服用的任何治疗糖尿病、高血压或其他疾病的药物。 如果你正在服用血液稀释剂，如华法林（Coumadin），需要额外做血液检查，以确保剂量合适。某些其他血液稀释剂则不需要这样做。 活动 你的医疗服务提供者可能会把你转介到心脏康复项目。在那里，你会学习如何慢慢增加运动量，以及如何照顾自己的心脏病。一定要避免提重物。 一定要了解心力衰竭和心脏病发作的警示信号。要知道在出现胸痛或心绞痛时该怎么做。 在重新开始性生活前，一定要先询问你的医疗服务提供者。未经同意，不要服用西地那非（Viagra）、伐地那非（Levitra）、他达拉非（Cialis）或任何治疗勃起问题的草药制剂。 确保你的家中环境安全、方便你活动，并能减少跌倒的风险。 如果你不能多走动，请向医疗服务提供者咨询可以在坐着时做的锻炼。 复查随访 一定要按照医疗服务提供者推荐的时间表接种流感疫苗和 COVID-19（新冠）疫苗（通常每年一次）。你可能还需要接种肺炎球菌疫苗（肺炎疫苗）。请向你的医疗服务提供者咨询。 ...

Back-Translation (to English):

Heart Failure - Discharge Instructions Heart failure is a disease in which the heart can no longer effectively pump oxygenated blood to the whole body. When symptoms become severe, hospitalization may be required. This article will explain what you need to do to take care of yourself after discharge. During your hospital stay You were hospitalized this time to treat heart failure. Heart failure means that the heart muscle becomes weak, or has difficulty relaxing, or has problems with both. Your heart is like a pump that sends fluid in the body throughout the whole body. Like any pump, if the output flow is insufficient, the fluid cannot flow well and will stay where it should not stay. In your body, this means fluid will accumulate in the lungs, abdomen, and legs. During your hospital stay: Your medical team will strictly regulate the amount of fluid you drink or that enters your body through intravenous infusion (IV). They will also observe and measure the amount of urine you pass. You may use medicines that help your body get rid of excess fluid. You may have some tests to understand how your heart is working. What to expect after you go home Your physical strength will slowly recover. When you first return home, you may need others to help take care of you. You may feel sad or emotionally low. These are all normal. Self-checks at home Every morning after getting up, weigh yourself on the same scale—before eating and after using the toilet. Each time you weigh yourself, try to wear similar clothing. Record your daily weight on a chart so you can easily see changes at any time. During the day, ask yourself: Is my energy level normal? Do I get short of breath more easily when doing daily activities? Have my clothes or shoes become tighter? Are my ankles or legs swollen? Am I coughing more often? When I cough, is the sound phlegmy and very wet? Do I get short of breath at night or when lying down? If you develop new (or different) symptoms, ask yourself...

Translation (Chinese (Simplified)):

心力衰竭 - 出院指导 心力衰竭是一种心脏无法有效地将富含氧气的血液泵送到身体其他部位的疾病。当症状变得严重时，可能需要住院治疗。本文讨论您出院后需要做些什么来照顾自己。 住院期间 您因心力衰竭接受治疗而住院。心力衰竭发生在心肌无力或难以放松，或两者兼有的情况下。 您的心脏是一个将液体泵送到全身的泵。与任何泵一样，如果泵的输出流量不足，液体就不能很好地流动，它们会滞留在不应该滞留的地方。在您的身体中，这意味着液体会积聚在您的肺部、腹部和腿部。 住院期间： 您的医疗团队密切调整了您饮用或通过静脉（IV）输液管接收的液体量。他们还监测和测量了您的尿量。 您可能接受了帮助身体排出多余液体的药物。 您可能接受了检查心脏功能的检测。 出院后的预期情况 您的体力会慢慢恢复。刚回家时，您可能需要帮助来照顾自己。您可能会感到悲伤或沮丧。所有这些都是正常的。 在家自我监测 每天早晨起床后，在同一台秤上称体重——在进食之前但在上厕所之后。确保每次称重时穿着类似的衣物。每天在图表上记录您的体重，以便跟踪。 在一天中，问问自己： 我的精力水平正常吗？ 在进行日常活动时，我是否比以前更容易气短？ 我的衣服或鞋子是否感觉变紧了？ 我的脚踝或腿部是否肿胀？ 我是否咳嗽更频繁了？我的咳嗽听起来是否有痰？ 我在夜间或躺下时是否气短？ 如果您有新的（或不同的）症状，问问自己： 我是否吃了与平常不同的东西或尝试了新的食物？ 我是否在正确的时间以正确的方式服用了所有药物？ 饮食和液体摄入 您的医疗保健提供者可能会要求您限制饮水量。 当您的心力衰竭不太严重时，您可能不需要过多限制液体摄入。 随着心力衰竭加重，您可能被要求将液体摄入限制在每天6至9杯（1.5至2升）。 您需要减少盐的摄入。盐会使您口渴，而口渴会导致您喝太多液体。额外的盐分也会使液体滞留在体内。许多尝起来不咸的食物，或您没有加盐的食物，实际上仍然含有大量的盐。 您可能需要服用利尿剂，或称排水药。 不要饮酒。酒精会使您的心肌更难工作。询问您的医疗提供者在有酒精和您需要避免的食物的特殊场合该怎么做。 如果您吸烟，请戒烟。如果需要，请寻求戒烟帮助。不要让任何人在您家中吸烟。 了解更多关于应该吃什么来使您的心脏和血管更健康的信息。 避免高脂肪食物。 远离快餐店。 避免一些预制食品和冷冻食品。 尽量远离让您感到压力的事物。如果您一直感到压力很大，或者您非常悲伤，请与您的医疗提供者交谈，他们可以为您推荐心理咨询师。 服用心脏药物 在回家之前，请将所有处方药配齐。按照医疗提供者告诉您的方式服药是非常重要的。未经医疗提供者同意，不要服用任何其他药物或草药。 用水服药。不要用西柚汁服药，因为它可能会改变您身体对某些药物的吸收方式。询问您的医疗提供者或药剂师这是否会对您造成问题。 以下药物通常会给心力衰竭患者使用。但有时可能因为某些原因而不适合服用。这些药物可能有助于保护您的心脏。如果您还没有服用以下任何药物，请与您的医疗提供者讨论： 抗血小板药物（血液稀释剂），如阿司匹林或氯吡格雷（波立维），帮助防止血液凝结 抗凝血药物（血液稀释剂），如华法林（香豆定），帮助防止血液凝结 β受体阻滞剂和ACE抑制剂药物以及其他降血压和治疗心肌的药物 他汀类或其他降胆固醇药物 在改变服药方式之前，请与您的医疗提供者交谈。切勿擅自停止服用这些心脏药物，或任何您可能正在服用的治疗糖尿病、高血压或其他疾病的药物。 如果您正在服用血液稀释剂，如华法林（香豆定），您需要进行额外的血液检查以确保剂量正确。某些其他血液稀释剂不需要这样做。 活动 您的医疗提供者可能会将您转介到心脏康复计划。在那里，您将学习如何逐渐增加运动量以及如何照顾您的心脏病。确保避免重物搬运。 确保您了解心力衰竭和心脏病发作的警告信号。了解当您有胸痛或心绞痛时该怎么做。 在恢复性生活之前，务必先咨询您的医疗提供者。未经事先检查，不要服用西地那非（伟哥）、伐地那非（艾力达）、他达拉非（希爱力）或任何用于勃起功能障碍的草药。 确保您的家居环境安全，便于您走动并避免跌倒。 如果您不能经常走动，请向您的医疗提供者咨询您可以坐着做的运动。 随访 确保按照您的医疗提供者建议的时间表（通常每年）接种流感疫苗和COVID-19疫苗。您可能还需要接种肺炎球菌疫苗（肺炎疫苗）。请向您的医疗提供者咨询。 您的医疗提供者可能会打电话给您，了解您的情况，并确保您在监测体重和服药。 您需要到医疗提供者的诊所进行随访预约。 您可能需要进行某些实验室检查来检测您的钠和钾水平，并监测您的肾脏功能。 何时联系医生 如果出现以下情况，请联系您的医疗提供者： 您一天内体重增加超过2磅（1公斤），或一周内增加5磅（2公斤）。 您感到非常疲劳和虚弱。 您感到头晕目...

Back-Translation (to English):

Heart Failure - Discharge Instructions Heart failure is a condition where the heart cannot effectively pump oxygen-rich blood to other parts of the body. When symptoms become severe, hospitalization may be required. This article discusses what you need to do to take care of yourself after discharge. During Hospitalization You were hospitalized for treatment of heart failure. Heart failure occurs when the heart muscle is weak or has difficulty relaxing, or both. Your heart is a pump that pumps fluid throughout your body. Like any pump, if the pump's output flow is insufficient, fluids cannot flow well, and they will stay in places where they should not stay. In your body, this means fluid will accumulate in your lungs, abdomen, and legs. During hospitalization: Your medical team closely adjusted the amount of fluid you drank or received through intravenous (IV) lines. They also monitored and measured your urine output. You may have received medications to help your body eliminate excess fluid. You may have received tests to check your heart function. What to Expect After Discharge Your physical strength will slowly recover. When you first return home, you may need help to take care of yourself. You may feel sad or depressed. All of this is normal. Self-Monitoring at Home Every morning after getting up, weigh yourself on the same scale — before eating but after using the toilet. Make sure to wear similar clothing each time you weigh yourself. Record your weight on a chart every day to track it. Throughout the day, ask yourself: Is my energy level normal? Am I more short of breath than before when doing daily activities? Do my clothes or shoes feel tighter? Are my ankles or legs swollen? Am I coughing more frequently? Does my cough sound like it has phlegm? Am I short of breath at night or when lying down? If you have new (or different) symptoms, ask yourself: Did I eat something different from usual or try new food? Did I take all my medications at the right ...

心力衰竭 - 出院 心力衰竭是指心脏无法再有效地将富含氧气的血液泵送到身体其他部位的状况。当症状变得严重时，可能需要住院治疗。本文讨论了您出院后需要做些什么来照顾自己。 **住院期间** 您住院是为了治疗心力衰竭。当您的心肌虚弱或难以放松，或者两者兼有时，就会发生心力衰竭。 您的心脏是一个将液体输送到全身的泵。就像任何泵一样，如果泵出的流量不足，液体的流动就会不顺畅，并滞留在不该停留的地方。在您的体内，这意味着液体会积聚在您的肺部、腹部和腿部。 在您住院期间： * 您的医疗团队密切调整了您饮用或通过静脉 (IV) 输液接收的液体量。他们还观察并测量了您的尿量。 * 您可能接受了药物治疗，以帮助身体排出多余的液体。 * 您可能做过检查，以确认心脏的工作情况。 **回家后的预期情况** 您的精力会慢慢恢复。刚回家时，您可能需要帮助来照顾自己。您可能会感到悲伤或抑郁。所有这些都是正常的。 **在家进行自我检查** 每天早上起床后——进食前但在上完厕所后——用同一个秤称重。确保每次称重时穿着相似的衣服。将您每天的体重记录在图表上，以便进行跟踪。 在一天中，问自己： * 我的精力水平正常吗？ * 做日常活动时，我是否感到更气短？ * 我的衣服或鞋子感觉紧吗？ * 我的脚踝或腿肿了吗？ * 我咳嗽的频率是否增加了？咳嗽听起来有痰（湿咳）吗？ * 晚上或躺下时，我会感到气短吗？ 如果您有新的（或不同的）症状，问自己： * 我是否吃了与平时不同的东西或尝试了新食物？ * 我是否在正确的时间以正确的方式服用了所有药物？ **饮食和液体** 您的医疗服务提供者可能会要求您限制饮水量。 * 当您的心力衰竭不是很严重时，您可能不需要过多限制液体摄入。 * 随着心力衰竭加重，您可能会被要求将液体限制在每天 6 到 9 杯（1.5 到 2 升）。 您需要少吃盐。盐会让您口渴，而口渴会导致您喝太多的液体。多余的盐分还会让液体滞留在体内。许多尝起来不咸或您没有加盐的食物，仍然含有大量的盐。 您可能需要服用利尿剂，或称“排水药” (water pill)。 不要饮酒。酒精会使心肌更难工作。询问您的提供者，在那些会供应酒精和您试图避免的食物的特殊场合该怎么做。 如果您吸烟，请戒烟。如果需要，请寻求戒烟帮助。不要让任何人在您家里吸烟。 了解更多关于应该吃什么来让心脏和血管更健康的信息。 * 避免高脂肪食物。 * 远离快餐店。 * 避免一些预制食品和冷冻食品。 尽量远离会让您感到压力的事情。如果您一直感到压力很大，或者非常悲伤，请与您的提供者交谈，他们可以将您转介给心理咨询师。 **服用心脏药物** 回家前请配好所有处方药。严格按照提供者的指示服药非常重要。在未咨询提供者之前，不要服用任何其他药物或草药。 用水送服药物。不要用葡萄柚汁（西柚汁）送服，因为它可能会改变身体吸收某些药物的方式。询问您的提供者或药剂师这对您是否会有问题。 以下药物通常提供给许多患有心力衰竭的人。但有时出于某种原因，服用它们可能不安全。这些药物可能有助于保护您的心脏。如果您尚未服用以下任何药物，请与您的提供者交谈： * 抗血小板药物（血液稀释剂），如阿司匹林 (aspirin) 或氯吡格雷 (clopidogrel [Plavix])，有助于防止血液凝固 * 抗凝药物（血液稀释剂），如华法林 (warfarin [Coumadin])，有助于防止血液凝固 * β受体阻滞剂 (Beta blocker) 和 ACE 抑制剂 (ACE inhibitor) 以及其他降低血压和治疗心肌的药物 * 他汀类药物 (Statins) 或其他降低胆固醇的药物 在改变服药方式之前，请先咨询您的提供者。切勿擅自停止服用这些心脏药物，或您因糖尿病、高血压或其他疾病正在服用的任何药物。 如果您正在服用血液稀释剂，如华法林 (Coumadin)，您需要进行额外的血液检查以确保剂量正确。其他一些血液稀释剂不需要这样做。 **活动** 您的提供者可能会将您转介到心脏康复计划。在那里，您将学习如何缓慢增加运动量以及如何护理您的心脏病。确保避免搬运重物。 确保您了解心力衰竭和心脏病发作的警示信号。知道当您出现胸痛或心绞痛 (angina) 时该怎么做。 在重新开始性生活之前，务必询问您的提供者。在未先确认的情况下，不要服用西地那非 (sildenafil [Viagra])、伐地那非 (vardenafil [Levitra])、他达拉非 (tadalafil [Cialis]) 或任何治疗勃起问题的草药。 确保您的家居布置安全且便于您走动，以避免跌倒。 如果您无法经常走动，请向您的提供者询...

Heart Failure - Discharge Heart failure refers to the condition where the heart can no longer effectively pump oxygen-rich blood to other parts of the body. When symptoms become severe, hospitalization may be required. This article discusses what you need to do to take care of yourself after you are discharged. **During the Hospital Stay** You were hospitalized to treat heart failure. Heart failure occurs when your heart muscle is weak or has difficulty relaxing, or both. Your heart is a pump that transports fluid throughout the body. Just like any pump, if the pumped flow is insufficient, the flow of fluid will not be smooth, and [it will] stay in places where it should not stay. In your body, this means fluid will accumulate in your lungs, abdomen, and legs. During your hospitalization: * Your medical team closely adjusted the amount of fluid you drank or received via intravenous (IV) infusion. They also observed and measured your urine output. * You may have received medication treatment to help the body expel excess fluid. * You may have done tests to confirm the heart's working condition. **What to Expect After Going Home** Your energy will recover slowly. When just returning home, you may need help to take care of yourself. You may feel sad or depressed. All of these are normal. **Self-Checks at Home** Every morning after getting up—before eating but after using the toilet—weigh yourself using the same scale. Ensure you wear similar clothes every time you weigh yourself. Record your daily weight on a chart for tracking. During the day, ask yourself: * Is my energy level normal? * When doing daily activities, do I feel more short of breath? * Do my clothes or shoes feel tight? * Are my ankles or legs swollen? * Has the frequency of my coughing increased? Does the cough sound like it has phlegm (wet cough)? * Do I feel short of breath at night or when lying down? If you have new (or different) symptoms, ask yourself: * Did I eat some...

Original English:

Taking warfarin Warfarin is a medicine that makes your blood less likely to form clots. It is important that you take warfarin exactly as you have been told. Changing how you take your warfarin, taking other medicines with it or at different times, and eating certain foods can change the way warfarin works in your body. If this happens, you may be more likely to form a clot or have bleeding problems. What to Expect at Home Warfarin is a medicine that makes your blood less likely to form clots. This may be important if: You have already had blood clots in your leg, arm, heart, or brain. Your health care provider is worried that a blood clot may form in your body. People who have a new heart valve, a large heart, a heart rhythm that is not normal, or other heart problems may need to take warfarin. When you are taking warfarin, you may be more likely to bleed, even from activities you have always done. Changing how you take your warfarin, taking other medicines, and eating certain foods all can change the way warfarin works in your body. If this happens, you may be more likely to form a clot or have bleeding problems. Taking Warfarin It is important that you take warfarin exactly as you have been told. Take only the dose your provider has prescribed. If you miss a dose, contact your provider for advice. If your pills look different from your last prescription, contact your provider or pharmacist right away. The tablets are different colors, depending on the dose. The dose is also marked on the pill. Your provider will test your blood at regular visits. This is called an INR test or sometimes a PT test. The test helps make sure you are taking the right amount of warfarin to help your body. Alcohol and some medicines can change how warfarin works in your body. DO NOT drink alcohol while you are taking warfarin. Talk with your provider before taking any other over-the-counter medicines, vitamins, supplements, cold medicines, antibiotics, or other medicines. Tell a...

服用华法林 华法林是一种让你的血液不容易形成血栓的药物。严格按照医护人员的嘱咐服用华法林非常重要。改变服药方法、同时服用其他药物或在不同时间服药，以及吃某些食物，都会改变华法林在你体内的作用。如果发生这些情况，你可能更容易形成血栓，或者出现出血问题。 在家中可以预期的情况 华法林是一种让你的血液不容易形成血栓的药物。如果出现以下情况，这可能很重要： 你已经在腿、手臂、心脏或大脑里得过血栓。 你的医疗服务提供者担心你的身体里可能会形成血栓。有新心脏瓣膜、心脏肥大、心律不齐或其他心脏问题的人，可能需要服用华法林。 当你在服用华法林时，你可能更容易出血，即使是你一直在做的日常活动。 改变你服用华法林的方式、服用其他药物以及吃某些食物，都会改变华法林在你体内的作用。如果发生这些情况，你可能更容易形成血栓，或者出现出血问题。 服用华法林 严格按照医护人员的嘱咐服用华法林非常重要。 只服用医护人员给你开的剂量。如果漏服一剂，请联系你的医护人员咨询。 如果你这次拿到的药片外观和上一次处方的不一样，请立刻联系你的医护人员或药师。华法林片剂会根据剂量不同而有不同的颜色。药片上也会标有剂量。 你的医护人员会在你定期复诊时给你抽血化验。这叫做 INR 检测，有时也叫 PT 检测。这个检测是为了确保你服用的华法林剂量对你的身体是合适的。 酒精和一些药物会改变华法林在你体内的作用。 服用华法林期间不要饮酒。 在服用任何其他非处方药、维生素、保健品、感冒药、抗生素或其他药物之前，先和你的医护人员沟通。 告诉所有给你看病的医护人员你正在服用华法林。这包括医生、护士和牙医。有时，在做某些操作或手术前，你可能需要停用或减少华法林剂量。在停药或改变剂量之前，一定要先咨询给你开华法林的那位医护人员。 询问是否需要佩戴写有你正在服用华法林的医疗警示手环或项链。这样，在紧急情况下照顾你的医护人员就会知道你正在服用这种药物。 你的饮食 有些食物会改变华法林在你体内的作用。在对饮食做出任何重大改变之前，一定要先咨询你的医护人员。 你不必完全避免这些食物，但要尽量少量食用或饮用。至少，不要在每天或每周之间大幅改变这些食物和制品的摄入量： 蛋黄酱和一些油，如菜籽油、橄榄油和大豆油 西兰花、抱子甘蓝和生的绿卷心菜 菊苣、生菜、菠菜、欧芹、西洋菜、大蒜和葱（青葱） 羽衣甘蓝、芥蓝、芥菜叶和芜菁叶 蔓越莓汁和绿茶 鱼油补充剂 用于花草茶中的草本植物 其他提示 因为服用华法林会让你比平时更容易出血： 你应避免可能导致受伤或皮肤破损的活动，比如对抗性运动。 使用软毛牙刷、上蜡牙线和电动剃须刀。接触锋利物品时要格外小心。 通过改善家中的照明、移除通道上的小地毯和电线来预防跌倒。不要伸手或攀爬去拿厨房里的物品。把东西放在你容易拿到的地方。避免在冰面、湿地板或其他湿滑或不熟悉的地面上行走。 一定要留意身体上是否有异常出血或淤青的迹象。 注意是否有牙龈出血、尿中带血、血便或黑便、流鼻血或呕血。 女性需要注意月经期间或两次月经之间是否有异常增多的出血。 可能会出现深红色或黑色的淤青。如果出现这种情况，请立刻联系你的医护人员。 何时联系医生 如果你出现以下情况，请联系你的医护人员： 严重摔倒，或头部受到撞击 注射或受伤部位出现疼痛、不适或肿胀 皮肤上出现大量淤青 大量出血（如频繁流鼻血或牙龈出血） 尿液或大便呈血色或深棕色 头痛、头晕或乏力 发烧或其他疾病，包括呕吐、腹泻或感染 你已经怀孕或计划怀孕

Taking Warfarin Warfarin is a medicine that makes it harder for your blood to form blood clots. It is very important to take warfarin exactly as instructed by your healthcare provider. Changing how you take the medicine, taking other medicines at the same time or taking it at different times, as well as eating certain foods, will all change how warfarin works in your body. If these situations occur, you may be more likely to form blood clots, or have bleeding problems. When you are taking warfarin, you may bleed more easily, even during daily activities you have always done. Changing how you take warfarin, taking other medicines, and eating certain foods will all change how warfarin works in your body. If these situations occur, you may be more likely to form blood clots, or have bleeding problems. Taking Warfarin Warfarin is a medication that makes your blood less likely to form blood clots. It is very important to take warfarin exactly as directed by your doctor. Changing the way you take warfarin, taking it with other medications or at different times, and eating certain foods can change the way warfarin works in your body. If this happens, you may be more likely to form blood clots or have bleeding problems. Home Care Instructions Warfarin is a medication that makes your blood less likely to form blood clots. This may be important if: You have had a blood clot in your leg, arm, heart, or brain. Your healthcare provider is concerned that blood clots may form in your body. People with a new heart valve, an enlarged heart, an irregular heartbeat, or other heart problems may need to take warfarin. When you take warfarin, you may bleed more easily, even from activities you have always been doing. Changing the way you take warfarin, taking other medications, and eating certain foods can change the way warfarin works in your body. If this happens, you may be more likely to form blood clots or have bleeding problems. Taking Warfarin It is very important to take warfarin exactly as directed by your doctor. Take only the dose prescribed by your doctor. If you miss a dose, contact your doctor for advice. If your pills look different from your last prescription, contact your doctor or pharmacist right away. Pills come in different colors depending on the dose. The dose is also marked on the pill. Your doctor will test your blood during regular visits. This is called an INR test, sometimes also called a PT test. This test helps ensure that the dose of warfarin you are taking is correct for your body. Alcohol and some medications can change the way warfarin works in your body. Taking warfarin Warfarin is a medicine that makes your blood less likely to form clots. It is important that you take warfarin exactly as you have been told. Item: EVAL_0052 | Document: CARD_003 | Model: Model C

Original English:

Heart attack – discharge A heart attack occurs when blood flow to a part of your heart is blocked long enough that part of the heart muscle is damaged or dies. This article discusses what you need to do to take care of yourself after you leave the hospital. When You're in the Hospital You were in the hospital because you had a heart attack. A heart attack occurs when blood flow to a part of your heart is blocked long enough that part of the heart muscle is damaged or dies. What to Expect at Home You may feel sad. You may feel anxious and as though you have to be very careful about what you do. All of these feelings are normal. They go away for most people after 2 or 3 weeks. You may also feel tired when you leave the hospital to go home. Activity You should know the signs and symptoms of angina. You may feel pressure, squeezing, burning, or tightness in your chest. You may also notice these symptoms in your arms, shoulders, neck, jaw, throat, or back. Some people also feel discomfort in their back, shoulders, and stomach area. You may have indigestion or feel sick to your stomach. You may feel tired and be short of breath, sweaty, lightheaded, or weak. You may have angina during physical activity, such as climbing stairs or walking uphill, lifting, sexual activity, or when you are out in cold weather. It can also happen when you are resting or it can wake you up when you are sleeping. Know how to treat your chest pain when it happens. Talk with your health care provider about what to do. Take it easy for the first 4 to 6 weeks after your heart attack. Avoid heavy lifting. Get some help with household chores if you can. Take 30 to 60 minutes to rest in the afternoon for first 4 to 6 weeks. Try to go to bed early and get plenty of sleep. Before starting to exercise, your provider may have you do an exercise test and recommend an exercise plan. This may happen before you leave the hospital or soon afterward. 心脏病发作 – 出院指导 心脏病发作是指流向心脏某一部分的血流被阻断时间过长，导致这部分心肌受损或坏死。本文将介绍出院后如何照顾自己。 在医院期间 您住院是因为发生了心脏病发作。心脏病发作是指流向心脏某一部分的血流被阻断时间过长，导致这部分心肌受损或坏死。 在家中可以预期的情况 您可能会感到伤心。您可能会感到焦虑，觉得自己做任何事都要非常小心。这些感觉都是正常的。对大多数人来说，这些感觉会在 2 到 3 周后消失。出院回家时，您也可能会感到疲劳。 活动 您应该了解心绞痛的体征和症状。 您可能会感到胸部有压迫感、挤压感、灼烧感或紧缩感。在手臂、肩膀、颈部、下颌、喉咙或背部也可能出现这些症状。 有些人还会感到背部、肩膀和腹部不适。 您可能会有消化不良，或感到恶心、反胃。 您可能会感到疲倦，并出现呼吸急促、出汗、头晕或乏力。 在进行体力活动时，您可能会出现心绞痛，例如爬楼梯、上坡行走、提重物、性生活，或在寒冷天气外出时。心绞痛也可能在您休息时发生，或在您睡觉时将您疼醒。 要知道在胸痛发生时如何处理。与您的医疗保健提供者讨论出现胸痛时应该怎么做。 心脏病发作后的前 4 到 6 周要放松休养。 避免提重物。如果可以，尽量请人帮忙做家务。 在前 4 到 6 周内，每天下午休息 30 到 60 分钟。尽量早点睡觉，保证充足睡眠。 在开始锻炼之前，您的医疗保健提供者可能会安排您做运动试验，并为您制定锻炼计划。这可能会在您出院前或出院后不久进行。在未与您的医疗保健提供者沟通前，不要自行改变锻炼计划。 您的医疗保健提供者可能会将您转介到心脏康复项目。在那里，您将学习如何逐渐增加运动量，以及如何照顾自己的心脏病。 如果您做过冠状动脉造影（angiography），请按照医疗保健提供者的指示护理穿刺部位。 在进行任何活动时，例如走路、摆放餐具、洗衣服，您都应该能轻松说话。如果不能，请停止该活动。 询问您的医疗保健提供者何时可以重返工作岗位。一般至少需要离开工作一周。 在进行性生活前，请先与您的医疗保健提供者沟通。询问何时可以重新开始。在未先咨询您的医疗保健提供者之前，不要服用 Viagra、Levitra、Cialis 或任何治疗勃起问题的草药制剂。 您需要等待多长时间才能恢复正常活动取决于： 心脏病发作前您的身体状况 这次心脏病发作的范围（大小） 是否出现并发症 您整体恢复的速度 饮食和生活方式 至少 2 周内不要饮酒。询问您的医疗保健提供者何时可以开始饮酒，以及对您来说安全的饮酒量和其他相关建议。 如果您吸烟，请戒烟。如果需要帮助戒烟，请向您的医疗保健提供者寻求帮助。不要让任何人在您家中吸烟，因为二手烟会伤害您。尽量远离让您感到压力大的事情。如果您总是感到压力很大，或者非常伤心，请与您的医疗保健提供者沟通。他们可以转介您去看心理咨询师。 进一步了解您应该如何饮食，来让心脏和血管更健康。 避免吃太咸的食物。 尽量不要去快餐店就餐。 按时服用心脏药物 在出院前把处方药配好。严格按照医疗保健提供者的嘱咐服药非常重要。在未先询问您的医疗保健提供者这些药物对您是否安全之前，不要服用任何其他药物或草药补充剂。 用水送服药物。不要用葡萄柚汁送服，因为葡萄柚汁可能会改变身体对某些药物的吸收方式。请向您的医疗保健提供者或药师咨询更多相关信息。 下面这些药物大多会在心脏病发作后给患者使用。但有时出于某些原因，这些药物可能对个别人来说并不安全。这些药物有助于预防再次发生心脏病发作。如果您目前没有服用以下任何一种药物，请与您的医疗保健提供者沟通： 抗血小板药物（blood thinners，血液稀释剂），如阿司匹林（aspirin）、氯吡格雷（clopidogrel，Plavix）、华法林（warfarin，Coumadin）、普拉格雷（prasugrel，Efient）或替格瑞洛（ticagrelor，Brilinta），帮助防止血液凝固 β 受体阻滞剂（Beta-blockers）和 ACE 抑制剂（ACE inhibitor）类药物，用于保护心脏 他汀类药物（Statins）或其他降胆固醇药物 钙通道阻滞剂（Calcium-channel blockers） 硝酸甘油（Nitroglycerin） 不要突然停用这些心脏药物。在未先与您的医疗保健提供者沟通之前，不要停用治疗糖尿病、高血压或您可能患有的其他疾病的药物。 如果您正在服用华法林（warfarin，Coumadin）等抗凝药（血液稀释剂），可能需要定期额外抽血检查，以确保剂量合适。 何时联系医生 如果您出现以下情况，请联系您的医疗保健提供者： 胸部、手臂、颈部或下颌出现疼痛、压迫感、紧缩感或沉重感 呼吸急促 胀气或消化不良 手臂麻木 出汗，或脸色变得苍白 头晕眼...

Back-Translation (to English):

Heart Attack – Discharge Instructions A heart attack means that the blood flow to a part of the heart is blocked for too long, causing that part of the heart muscle to be damaged or to die. This article will explain how to take care of yourself after discharge. During your hospital stay You were hospitalized because you had a heart attack. A heart attack means that the blood flow to a part of the heart is blocked for too long, causing that part of the heart muscle to be damaged or to die. What to expect at home You may feel sad. You may feel anxious and feel that you must be very careful doing anything. These feelings are all normal. For most people, these feelings go away after 2 to 3 weeks. You may also feel tired when you are discharged and go home. Activity You should understand the signs and symptoms of angina. You may feel pressure, squeezing, burning, or tightness in your chest. These symptoms may also appear in your arm, shoulder, neck, jaw, throat, or back. Some people also feel discomfort in the back, shoulders, and abdomen. You may have indigestion, or feel nauseated or queasy. You may feel tired and have shortness of breath, sweating, dizziness, or weakness. You may have angina when doing physical activity, such as climbing stairs, walking uphill, lifting heavy objects, having sex, or going out in cold weather. Angina may also occur when you are resting, or may wake you from sleep with pain. Know what to do when chest pain occurs. Discuss with your health care provider what you should do if you develop chest pain. You should rest and take it easy for the first 4 to 6 weeks after a heart attack. Avoid lifting heavy objects. If possible, try to have someone help you with housework. Rest for 30 to 60 minutes every afternoon during the first 4 to 6 weeks. Try to go to bed early and ensure adequate sleep. Before you start exercising, your health care provider may arrange an exercise test for you and develop an exercise plan for you....

You may have indigestion or feel sick to your stomach. You may feel tired and be short of breath, sweaty, lightheaded, or weak. 心脏病发作 – 出院 当流向心脏某部分的血流受阻时间过长，导致该部分心肌受损或坏死时，就会发生心脏病发作。本文讨论了您出院后需要做些什么来照顾自己。 **在医院期间** 您住院是因为心脏病发作。当流向心脏某部分的血流受阻时间过长，导致该部分心肌受损或坏死时，就会发生心脏病发作。 **回家后的预期情况** 您可能会感到难过。您可能会感到焦虑，觉得自己在做任何事情时都必须非常小心。所有这些感觉都是正常的。对于大多数人来说，这些感觉会在 2 到 3 周后消失。出院回家时，您也可能会感到疲倦。 **活动** 您应该了解心绞痛的体征和症状。 * 您可能会感到胸部有压迫感、挤压感、烧灼感或紧绷感。您也可能会在手臂、肩膀、颈部、下巴、喉咙或背部注意到这些症状。 * 有些人还会感到背部、肩膀和胃部区域不适。 * 您可能会消化不良或感到恶心（胃部不适）。 * 您可能会感到疲倦、气短、出汗、头晕或虚弱。 * 您可能会在进行体力活动（如爬楼梯或上坡行走、提重物、性生活）或在寒冷天气外出时出现心绞痛。它也可能在您休息时发生，或者在睡觉时把您疼醒。 * 了解发生胸痛时该如何处理。请与您的医疗服务提供者讨论该怎么做。 在心脏病发作后的最初 4 到 6 周内要多注意休息。 * 避免提重物。如果可以，请人帮忙做家务。 * 在最初的 4 到 6 周内，下午要休息 30 到 60 分钟。尽量早睡，保证充足的睡眠。 * 在开始锻炼之前，您的医疗服务提供者可能会让您做一项运动测试，并推荐一个锻炼计划。这可能会在您出院前或出院后不久进行。在与您的医疗服务提供者交谈之前，请勿更改您的锻炼计划。 * 您的医疗服务提供者可能会将您转介到心脏康复计划。在那里，您将学习如何缓慢增加运动量以及如何护理您的心脏病。 * 如果您做了血管造影术，请按照医疗服务提供者的指示护理穿刺部位。 * 在做任何活动（如散步、摆餐具和洗衣服）时，您应该能够轻松地交谈。如果不能，请停止活动。 询问您的医疗服务提供者何时可以重返工作岗位。预计至少要休假一周。 在进行性生活之前，请咨询您的医疗服务提供者。询问何时可以恢复性生活。在未咨询医疗服务提供者之前，请勿服用伟哥 (Viagra)、艾力达 (Levitra)、希爱力 (Cialis) 或任何治疗勃起问题的草药。 您需要等待多久才能恢复正常活动取决于： * 您心脏病发作前的身体状况 * 心脏病发作的范围大小 * 您是否出现了并发症 * 您的整体恢复速度 **饮食和生活方式** 至少 2 周内不要饮酒。询问您的医疗服务提供者何时可以开始饮酒，以及关于多少饮酒量对您是安全的指导。 如果您吸烟，请戒烟。如果需要，请向您的医疗服务提供者寻求戒烟帮助。不要让任何人在您家中吸烟，因为二手烟会伤害您。尽量远离会让您感到压力的事情。如果您一直感到有压力，或者感到非常难过，请与您的医疗服务提供者交谈。他们可以将您转介给心理咨询师。 了解更多关于应该吃什么来让您的心脏和血管更健康的信息。 * 避免吃咸的食物。 * 远离快餐店。 **服用心脏药物** 在回家之前配好药。严格按照医疗服务提供者的指示服药非常重要。在未询问医疗服务提供者是否安全之前，请勿服用任何其他药物或草药补充剂。 用水送服药物。不要用葡萄柚汁（西柚汁）送服，因为它可能会改变身体吸收某些药物的方式。请向您的医疗服务提供者或药剂师咨询有关此方面的更多信息。 大多数人在心脏病发作后都会服用以下药物。不过，有时出于某种原因，服用这些药物可能不安全。这些药物有助于预防再次心脏病发作。如果您尚未服用以下任何药物，请与您的医疗服务提供者交谈： * 抗血小板药物（血液稀释剂），如阿司匹林 (aspirin)、氯吡格雷 (Plavix)、华法林 (Coumadin)、普拉格雷 (Efient) 或替格瑞洛 (Brilinta)，以帮助防止血液凝固 * β-受体阻滞剂和 ACE 抑制剂药物，以帮助保护您的心脏 * 他汀类药物或其他降低胆固醇的药物 * 钙通道阻滞剂 * 硝酸甘油 不要突然停止服用这些心脏药物。在未与您的医疗服务提供者交谈之前，请勿停止服用治疗糖尿病、高血压或您可能患有的任何其他疾病的药物。 如果您正在服用华法林 (Coumadin) 等血液稀释剂，您可能需要定期进行额外的血液检查，以确保剂量正确。 **何时致电医生** 如果您有以下感觉，请联系您的医疗服务提供者： * 胸部、手臂、颈部或下巴感到疼痛、压迫、紧绷或沉重 * 气短（呼吸急促） * 胀气痛或消化不良 * 手臂麻木 * 出汗，或者面色苍白 * 头晕 心绞痛的变化可能意味着您的心脏病正在恶化。...

This article discusses what you need to do to take care of yourself after you are discharged. **While in the Hospital** You were hospitalized because of a heart attack. A heart attack occurs when blood flow to a certain part of the heart is blocked for too long, causing that part of the heart muscle to be damaged or die. **What to Expect After Going Home** You may feel sad. You may feel anxious, feeling that you must be very careful when doing anything. All these feelings are normal. For most people, these feelings will disappear after 2 to 3 weeks. You may also feel tired when you are discharged home. **Activity** You should understand the signs and symptoms of angina. * You may feel pressure, squeezing, burning, or tightness in your chest. You may also notice these symptoms in your arms, shoulders, neck, jaw, throat, or back. * Some people also feel discomfort in the back, shoulders, and stomach area. * You may have indigestion or feel nauseous (upset stomach). * You may feel tired, short of breath, sweaty, dizzy, or weak. * You may experience angina when doing physical activity (such as climbing stairs or walking uphill, lifting heavy objects, sexual activity) or going out in cold weather. It may also happen while you are resting, or wake you up from sleep with pain. * Know what to do when chest pain occurs. Please discuss with your healthcare provider what to do. Pay more attention to resting during the first 4 to 6 weeks after a heart attack. * Avoid lifting heavy objects. If possible, ask someone to help with housework. * During the first 4 to 6 weeks, rest for 30 to 60 minutes in the afternoon. Item: EVAL_0076 | Document: CARD_004 | Model: Model C

Original English:

High blood pressure - what to ask your doctor When your heart pumps blood into your arteries, the pressure of the blood against the artery walls is called your blood pressure. Your blood pressure is given as two numbers: systolic over diastolic blood pressure. Your systolic blood pressure is the highest blood pressure during the course of your heart beat cycle. Your diastolic blood pressure is the lowest pressure. When your blood pressure gets too high, it puts extra stress on your heart and blood vessels. If your blood pressure stays high all the time, you will be at a higher risk for heart attacks and other vascular (blood vessel) diseases, strokes, kidney disease, and other health problems. Below are questions you may want to ask your health care provider to help you take care of your blood pressure. Questions How can I change the way I live to lower my blood pressure? What is a heart-healthy diet? Is it OK to ever eat something that is not heart healthy? What are some ways to eat healthy when I go to a restaurant? Do I need to limit how much salt I use? Are there other spices that I can use to make my food taste good? Is it OK to drink alcohol? How much is OK? What can I do to stop smoking? Is it OK to be around other people who are smoking? Should I check my blood pressure at home? What type of equipment should I buy? Where can I learn how to use it? How often do I need to check my blood pressure? Should I write it down and bring it to my next visit? If I cannot check my own blood pressure, where else can I have it checked? What should my blood pressure reading be? Should I rest before taking my blood pressure? When should I contact my provider? What is my cholesterol? Do I need to take medicines for it? Is it OK to be sexually active? Is it safe to use sildenafil (Viagra), or tadalafil (Cialis), vardenafil (Staxyn), or avanafil (Stendra) for erection problems? What medicines am I taking to treat high blood pressure? Do they have any side effects? What...

高血压 - 要问医生什么 当心脏把血液泵入动脉时，血液对动脉壁产生的压力就叫做血压。血压用两个数字来表示：收缩压在上，舒张压在下。收缩压是心脏一次跳动过程中最高的血压。舒张压是最低的血压。 当血压过高时，会给心脏和血管带来额外的压力。如果血压一直偏高，您发生心脏病发作和其他血管疾病、中风、肾脏疾病以及其他健康问题的风险会更高。 下面是一些您可以问您的医疗服务提供者的问题，帮助您更好地控制血压。 问题 我怎样改变生活方式来降低血压？ 什么是有益心脏健康的饮食？偶尔吃一些对心脏不太健康的食物可以吗？我去餐馆时，有哪些健康饮食的方法？ 我需要限制吃盐的量吗？还有哪些调味品可以用来让食物更好吃？ 可以喝酒吗？喝多少算合适？ 我可以做些什么来戒烟？在别人吸烟的环境里可以吗？ 我需要在家里自己量血压吗？ 我应该买哪种血压测量设备？我可以在哪里学习如何使用它？ 我需要多久量一次血压？我是否应该把读数记下来，并带到下次就诊时给医生看？ 如果我不能自己量血压，还有哪里可以帮我量血压？ 我的血压应该控制在多少？在量血压前需要先休息吗？ 我什么时候应该联系医生？ 我的胆固醇是多少？我需要为此服用药物吗？ 可以有性生活吗？使用西地那非（Viagra 万艾可）、他达拉非（Cialis 希爱力）、伐地那非（Staxyn），或阿伐那非（Stendra）来治疗勃起问题安全吗？ 我正在服用哪些治疗高血压的药物？ 这些药物有副作用吗？如果我漏服了一次该怎么办？ 我自己擅自停用这些药物，什么时候是安全的？ 我可以做多少活动量？ 在运动前，我需要做运动负荷试验（压力测试）吗？ 我自己一个人运动安全吗？ 我应该在室内还是室外运动？ 我应该从哪些活动开始？有没有对我来说不安全的活动或锻炼？ 我可以运动多长时间、强度多大？ 有哪些警告信号提示我应该停止运动？

高血压——该向医生问些什么 当您的心脏将血液泵入动脉时，血液对动脉壁产生的压力称为血压。您的血压由两个数字组成：收缩压和舒张压。收缩压是心跳周期中的最高血压值。舒张压是最低血压值。 当您的血压过高时，会给心脏和血管带来额外的负担。如果您的血压一直居高不下，您患心脏病发作、其他血管（血管）疾病、中风、肾脏疾病以及其他健康问题的风险就会增加。 以下是您可以向医疗服务提供者咨询的一些问题，以帮助您控制血压。 问题 我该如何改变生活方式来降低血压？ * 什么是心脏健康饮食？偶尔吃一些对心脏不健康的食物可以吗？去餐馆吃饭时，有哪些健康饮食的方法？ * 我需要限制盐的摄入量吗？我可以使用其他香料来给食物提味吗？ * 可以喝酒吗？喝多少是可以的？ * 我该怎么做才能戒烟？待在吸烟的人周围可以吗？ 我应该在家测量血压吗？ * 我应该购买哪种类型的设备？我在哪里可以学习如何使用它？ * 我需要多久测量一次血压？我应该把它记录下来并在下次就诊时带给您看吗？ * 如果我无法自己测量血压，还有哪里可以测量？ * 我的血压读数应该是多少？测量血压前我应该休息吗？ * 我应该在什么时候联系我的医疗服务提供者？ * 我的胆固醇是多少？我需要为此服药吗？ 进行性生活可以吗？使用西地那非 (Viagra)、他达拉非 (Cialis)、伐地那非 (Staxyn) 或阿伐那非 (Stendra) 来治疗勃起问题安全吗？ 我正在服用哪些药物来治疗高血压？ * 它们有什么副作用吗？如果我漏服了一次药该怎么办？ * 我自己停用任何这些药物是否安全？ 我可以做多少活动？ * 运动前我需要做运动负荷测试（压力测试）吗？ * 我独自运动安全吗？ * 我应该在室内还是室外运动？ * 我应该从哪些活动开始？有哪些活动或运动对我来说是不安全的？ * 我可以运动多久？强度可以多大？ * 出现哪些警示信号时我应该停止运动？

High Blood Pressure — What to Ask Your Doctor When your heart pumps blood into the arteries, the pressure produced by the blood against the artery walls is called blood pressure. Your blood pressure is composed of two numbers: systolic pressure and diastolic pressure. Systolic pressure is the highest blood pressure value during the heartbeat cycle. Diastolic pressure is the lowest blood pressure value. When your blood pressure is too high, it brings extra burden to the heart and blood vessels. If your blood pressure stays high all the time, your risk of suffering from heart attack, other vascular (blood vessel) diseases, stroke, kidney disease, and other health problems will increase. Below are some questions you can ask your healthcare provider to help you control blood pressure. Questions How should I change my lifestyle to lower blood pressure? * What is a heart-healthy diet? Can I use other spices to add flavor to food? * Is it okay to drink alcohol? How much is okay to drink? * What should I do to quit smoking? Is it okay to stay around people who smoke? Should I measure blood pressure at home? * What type of device should I buy? Where can I learn how to use it? * How often do I need to measure blood pressure? Should I record it and bring it to show you at the next visit? * If I cannot measure blood pressure myself, where else can it be measured? * What should my blood pressure reading be? Should I rest before measuring blood pressure? * When should I contact my healthcare provider? * What is my cholesterol? Do I need to take medicine for this? Is it okay to have a sex life? It can damage your organs. It can also lead to heart attacks or strokes as well as many other health problems. You can take measures to control symptoms, prevent damage caused by diabetes, and improve your quality of life. Below are some questions you can ask healthcare providers to help you manage diabetes. **Questions** Ask the healthcare provider to check the nerves, skin, and pulse of your feet. You can also ask the following questions: * How often should I check my feet? What should I do when checking? What problems should I call the doctor about if they appear? * Who should help me trim my toenails? Is it okay if I trim them myself? * How should I care for my feet every day? What kind of shoes and socks should I wear? * Should I go see a podiatrist (foot doctor)? Ask the healthcare provider questions about exercise, including: * Before starting exercise, do I need to check my heart? What about eyes? What about feet? * What kind of exercise plan should I follow? Which activities should be avoided? * When should I check blood sugar while exercising? What should I carry with me while exercising? Should I eat before or during exercise? Do I need to adjust medication while exercising? When should I next see an eye doctor (optometrist or ophthalmologist) to check my eyes? What eye problems should I contact the eye doctor about if they appear? Ask the healthcare provider about seeing a dietitian. Questions for the dietitian may include: * Which foods are most likely to raise my blood sugar? * Which foods help me achieve my weight loss goals? Ask the healthcare provider questions about diabetes medications: * When should I take the medicine? * What should I do if I miss a dose? * Are there any side effects? Item: EVAL_0124 | Document: DIAB_002 | Model: Model C

Original English:

Low blood sugar - self-care Low blood sugar is a condition that occurs when your blood sugar (glucose) is lower than normal. Low blood sugar may occur in people with diabetes who are taking insulin or certain other medicines to control their diabetes. Low blood sugar can cause dangerous symptoms. Learn how to recognize the symptoms of low blood sugar and how to prevent them. What is Low Blood Sugar? Low blood sugar is called hypoglycemia. A blood sugar level below 70 mg/dL (3.9 mmol/L) is low and can harm you. A blood sugar level below 54 mg/dL (3.0 mmol/L) is a cause for immediate action. You are at risk for low blood sugar if you have diabetes and are taking any of the following diabetes medicines: Insulin Glyburide (Micronase), glipizide (Glucotrol), glimepiride (Amaryl), repaglinide (Prandin), or nateglinide (Starlix) You are also at increased risk of having low blood sugar if you have had previous low blood sugar levels. Recognizing Low Blood Sugar Know how to tell when your blood sugar is getting low. Symptoms include: Weakness or feeling tired Shaking Sweating Headache Hunger Feeling uneasy, nervous, or anxious Feeling cranky Trouble thinking clearly Double or blurry vision Fast or pounding heartbeat Sometimes your blood sugar may be too low even if you do not have symptoms. If it gets too low, you may: Faint Have a seizure Go into a coma Some people who have had diabetes for a long time stop being able to sense low blood sugar. This is called hypoglycemic unawareness. Ask your health care provider if wearing a continuous glucose monitor and sensor can help you detect when your blood sugar is getting too low in order to help prevent symptoms. Check Your Blood Sugar Often Talk with your provider about when you should check your blood sugar every day. People who have low blood sugar need to check their blood sugar more often. The most common causes of low blood sugar are: Taking your insulin or diabetes medicine at the wrong time Taking too much insul...

Translation (Chinese (Simplified)):

低血糖 - 自我护理 低血糖是指当你的血糖（葡萄糖）低于正常水平时出现的一种情况。低血糖可能发生在使用胰岛素或某些其他药物来控制糖尿病的糖尿病患者身上。低血糖可以引起危险的症状。请学习如何识别低血糖的症状以及如何预防它们。 什么是低血糖？ 低血糖的医学名称是低血糖症（hypoglycemia）。血糖低于 70 mg/dL（3.9 mmol/L）就是偏低，可能会伤害你的身体。血糖低于 54 mg/dL（3.0 mmol/L）时，需要立刻采取措施。 如果你有糖尿病，并正在使用以下任何一种糖尿病药物，你就有发生低血糖的风险： 胰岛素 格列本脲（Glyburide，Micronase）、格列吡嗪（glipizide，Glucotrol）、格列美脲（glimepiride，Amaryl）、瑞格列奈（repaglinide，Prandin）或那格列奈（nateglinide，Starlix） 如果你以前发生过低血糖，你发生低血糖的风险也会增加。 识别低血糖 要知道如何判断你的血糖正在变低。症状包括： - 虚弱或感到疲劳 - 发抖 - 出汗 - 头痛 - 饥饿 - 感到不安、紧张或焦虑 - 容易发脾气 - 思考不清楚 - 复视或视力模糊 - 心跳加快或心慌 有时，即使你没有症状，你的血糖也可能过低。如果血糖降得太低，你可能会： - 昏厥 - 抽搐（癫痫发作） - 进入昏迷 有些患糖尿病很久的人会失去感知低血糖的能力。这叫做低血糖无感知（hypoglycemic unawareness）。询问你的医疗服务提供者，佩戴连续血糖监测仪（continuous glucose monitor）和传感器是否可以帮助你在血糖过低之前发现，从而帮助预防症状。 经常检查血糖 与你的医疗服务提供者讨论，你每天应该在什么时候检查血糖。发生低血糖的人需要更频繁地检查血糖。 最常见的低血糖原因包括： - 在错误的时间注射胰岛素或服用糖尿病药物 - 注射过多的胰岛素或服用过多的糖尿病药物 - 为纠正高血糖注射了胰岛素，但没有进食 - 在已经注射胰岛素或服用糖尿病药物后，正餐或加餐吃得不够 - 不吃正餐（这可能意味着你的长效胰岛素剂量过高，应与医疗服务提供者沟通） - 服药后等太久才吃饭 - 运动量很大，或在你平时不常运动的时间运动 - 在运动前不检查血糖，或不根据运动调整胰岛素剂量 - 饮酒 预防低血糖 预防低血糖要比事后治疗好。随身携带一种起效快的糖分来源。 - 当你运动时，要检查血糖水平。确保你随身带有零食。 - 与医疗服务提供者讨论，在你运动的日子是否需要减少胰岛素剂量。 - 询问医疗服务提供者，你是否需要睡前加餐来预防夜间低血糖。含蛋白质的零食可能更好。 - 不要空腹饮酒。女性每天饮酒应限制在 1 杯以内，男性每天饮酒应限制在 2 杯以内。 家人和朋友应当知道如何帮助你。他们应当了解： - 低血糖的症状，以及如何判断你是否出现这些症状。 - 需要给你吃多少、哪一种食物。 - 什么时候需要呼叫急救。 - 如何注射胰高血糖素（glucagon），这是一种可以升高血糖的激素。你的医疗服务提供者会告诉你何时使用这种药物。 如果你有糖尿病，应始终佩戴医疗警示手环或项链。这可以帮助急救人员知道你有糖尿病。 当你的血糖变低时 每当你有低血糖症状时，都要检查血糖。如果血糖低于 70 mg/dL，立刻进行处理。 1. 吃一些含大约 15 克（g）碳水化合物的食物。例如： - 4 片葡萄糖片 - 半杯（4 盎司或 120 mL）果汁或普通含糖汽水（非无糖） - 5 或 6 颗硬糖 - 1 汤匙（tbsp）或 15 mL 白糖，可直接吃或溶于水中 - 1 汤匙（15 mL）蜂蜜或糖浆 2. 等大约 15 分钟再吃别的东西。注意不要吃太多，否则会导致高血糖和体重增加。 3. 再次检查你的血糖。 4. 如果 15 分钟后你仍然感觉不好，并且血糖仍低于 70 mg/dL（3.9 mmol/L），再吃一份含 15 克碳水化合物的零食。 如果你的血糖已经在较安全的范围——高于 70 mg/dL（3.9 mmol/L）——而且距离下一餐还有一个多小时，你可能需要吃一份同时含有碳水化合物和蛋白质的零食。 询问你的医疗服务提供者如何处理这种情况。如果这些升高血糖的步骤没有效果，立刻联系你的医疗服务提供者。 与医生或护士沟通 如果你使用胰岛素，而且你的血糖经常或持续偏低，询问你的医疗服务提供者或护士你是否需要： - 纠正你的胰岛素注射方法 - 更换不同类型的针头 ...

Back-Translation (to English):

Hypoglycemia - Self-care Hypoglycemia is a condition that occurs when your blood sugar (glucose) is lower than normal. Hypoglycemia can occur in people with diabetes who use insulin or certain other medicines to control diabetes. Hypoglycemia can cause dangerous symptoms. Learn how to recognize the symptoms of hypoglycemia and how to prevent them. What is hypoglycemia? The medical name for low blood sugar is hypoglycemia. Blood sugar below 70 mg/dL (3.9 mmol/L) is low and may harm your body. When blood sugar is below 54 mg/dL (3.0 mmol/L), you need to take action immediately. If you have diabetes and are using any of the following diabetes medicines, you are at risk of hypoglycemia: Insulin Glyburide (Micronase), glipizide (Glucotrol), glimepiride (Amaryl), repaglinide (Prandin), or nateglinide (Starlix) If you have had hypoglycemia before, your risk of hypoglycemia will also increase. Recognizing hypoglycemia Know how to tell when your blood sugar is getting low. Symptoms include: - Weakness or feeling tired - Shaking - Sweating - Headache - Hunger - Feeling uneasy, nervous, or anxious - Being easily irritable - Thinking unclearly - Double vision or blurred vision - Rapid heartbeat or palpitations Sometimes, your blood sugar may be too low even if you have no symptoms. If blood sugar drops too low, you may: - Faint - Have convulsions (seizures) - Go into a coma Some people who have had diabetes for a long time lose the ability to sense hypoglycemia. This is called hypoglycemic unawareness. Ask your health care provider whether wearing a continuous glucose monitor and sensor can help you detect when your blood sugar is too low before it happens, thereby helping to prevent symptoms. Check blood sugar often Talk with your health care provider about when you should check your blood sugar each day. People who have hypoglycemia need to check their blood sugar more often. 低血糖 - 自我护理 低血糖是指您的血糖（葡萄糖）低于正常水平的一种状况。低血糖可能发生在正在使用胰岛素或某些其他药物控制糖尿病的糖尿病患者身上。低血糖可能导致危险症状。了解如何识别低血糖症状以及如何预防它们。 什么是低血糖？ 低血糖被称为低血糖症。血糖水平低于 70 mg/dL（3.9 mmol/L）属于偏低，可能对您造成伤害。血糖水平低于 54 mg/dL（3.0 mmol/L）需要立即采取行动。 如果您患有糖尿病并正在服用以下任何糖尿病药物，您就有发生低血糖的风险： 胰岛素 格列本脲（Micronase）、格列吡嗪（Glucotrol）、格列美脲（Amaryl）、瑞格列奈（Prandin）或那格列奈（Starlix） 如果您以前曾有过低血糖，您发生低血糖的风险也会增加。 识别低血糖 了解如何判断您的血糖正在变低。症状包括： 虚弱或感到疲倦 颤抖 出汗 头痛 饥饿 感到不安、紧张或焦虑 感到烦躁 思维不清晰 视物重影或模糊 心跳加快或剧烈跳动 有时即使您没有症状，您的血糖也可能过低。如果血糖过低，您可能会： 晕厥 癫痫发作 陷入昏迷 一些患糖尿病多年的人会失去感知低血糖的能力。这被称为低血糖无感知。请咨询您的医疗保健提供者，佩戴持续血糖监测仪和传感器是否可以帮助您检测血糖何时变得过低，以帮助预防症状。 经常检查您的血糖 与您的医疗提供者讨论您每天应该在什么时候检查血糖。有低血糖的人需要更频繁地检查血糖。 低血糖最常见的原因是： 在错误的时间服用胰岛素或糖尿病药物 服用过多的胰岛素或糖尿病药物 使用胰岛素纠正高血糖但没有进食任何食物 在使用胰岛素或糖尿病药物后，用餐或吃点心时吃得不够 不吃饭（这可能意味着您的长效胰岛素剂量过高，因此您应该与您的医疗提供者讨论） 服药后等待太久才吃饭 大量运动或在不寻常的时间运动 运动前没有检查血糖或没有调整胰岛素剂量 饮酒 预防低血糖 预防低血糖比治疗它更好。始终随身携带速效糖来源。 运动时，检查您的血糖水平。确保您随身携带点心。 与您的医疗提供者讨论在运动日减少胰岛素剂量。 询问您的医疗提供者您是否需要睡前点心来预防夜间低血糖。蛋白质点心可能是最好的选择。 不要在不吃食物的情况下饮酒。女性应将饮酒限制在每天1杯，男性应将饮酒限制在每天2杯。家人和朋友应该知道如何帮助。他们应该知道： 低血糖的症状以及如何判断您是否有这些症状。 他们应该给您多少以及什么类型的食物。 何时拨打急救电话。 如何注射胰高血糖素，一种提高血糖的激素。您的医疗提供者会告诉您何时使用这种药物。 如果您患有糖尿病，请始终佩戴医疗警示手环或项链。这有助于急救医务人员知道您患有糖尿病。 当您的血糖变低时 每当您出现低血糖症状时，请检查您的血糖。如果您的血糖低于 70 mg/dL，请立即自我处理。 1. 吃一些含有约 15 克（g）碳水化合物的食物。例如： 4 片葡萄糖片 半杯（4 盎司或 120 毫升）果汁或普通非无糖汽水 5 或 6 颗硬糖 1 汤匙（tbsp）或 15 毫升糖，纯糖或溶于水中 1 汤匙（15 毫升）蜂蜜或糖浆 2. 等待约 15 分钟后再吃更多食物。小心不要吃太多。这可能导致高血糖和体重增加。 3. 再次检查您的血糖。 4. 如果 15 分钟后您感觉没有好转，且血糖仍低于 70 mg/dL（3.9 mmol/L），请再吃一份含有 15 克碳水化合物的点心。 如果您的血糖处于较安全的范围——高于 70 mg/dL（3.9 mmol/L）——且距离下一餐超过一小时，您可能需要吃一份含有碳水化合物和蛋白质的点心。 请咨询您的医疗提供者如何处理这种情况。如果这些提高血糖的步骤不起作用，请立即联系您的医疗提供者。 与您的医生或护士交谈 如果您使用胰岛素且血糖经常或持续偏低，请询问您的医疗提供者或护士您是否： 胰岛素注射方法是否正确 是否需要不同类型的针头 是否应该改变胰岛素用量 是否应该更换胰岛素种类 在未与您的医疗提供者或护士交谈之前，不要做任何改变。 有时低血糖可能是由于意外服用了错误的药物。请与您的药剂师核对您的药物。 何时就医 如果在您吃了含糖点心后低血糖的症状没有改善，请让人开车送您去急诊室或拨打 911 或当地急救电话。血糖低时不要开车。 如果低血糖患者不清醒或无法被唤醒，请立即寻求医疗帮助，因为这是医疗紧急情况。

低血糖 —— 自我护理 低血糖是指您的血糖（葡萄糖）低于正常水平的情况。低血糖可能发生在患有糖尿病并正在服用胰岛素或其他某些药物来控制糖尿病的人身上。低血糖会导致危险的症状。了解如何识别低血糖的症状以及如何预防它们。 **什么是低血糖？** 低血糖在医学上称为低血糖症（Hypoglycemia）。血糖水平低于 70 mg/dL (3.9 mmol/L) 即为偏低，可能会对您造成伤害。血糖水平低于 54 mg/dL (3.0 mmol/L) 则需要立即采取行动。 如果您患有糖尿病并正在服用以下任何一种糖尿病药物，您就有发生低血糖的风险： * 胰岛素 (Insulin) * 格列本脲 (Micronase)、格列吡嗪 (Glucotrol)、格列美脲 (Amaryl)、瑞格列奈 (Prandin) 或那格列奈 (Starlix) 如果您以前出现过低血糖水平，您发生低血糖的风险也会增加。 **识别低血糖** 了解如何判断您的血糖何时变低。症状包括： * 虚弱或感到疲倦 * 颤抖 * 出汗 * 头痛 * 饥饿 * 感到不安、紧张或焦虑 * 脾气暴躁 * 思维不清 * 重影（复视）或视力模糊 * 心跳加快或剧烈跳动 有时，即使您没有症状，您的血糖也可能过低。如果血糖过低，您可能会： * 晕厥 * 癫痫发作 * 陷入昏迷 一些患糖尿病很长时间的人不再能感觉到低血糖。这被称为低血糖无察觉症（hypoglycemic unawareness）。请咨询您的医疗保健提供者，佩戴连续血糖监测仪和传感器是否可以帮助您检测血糖何时过低，从而帮助预防症状。 **经常检测血糖** 与您的提供者讨论您每天应该何时检测血糖。患有低血糖的人需要更频繁地检测血糖。 低血糖最常见的原因是： * 在错误的时间服用胰岛素或糖尿病药物 * 服用过多的胰岛素或糖尿病药物 * 注射胰岛素纠正高血糖但未进食任何食物 * 服用胰岛素或糖尿病药物后，正餐或零食吃得不够 * 不吃饭（这可能意味着您的长效胰岛素剂量过高，因此您应该与您的提供者谈谈） * 服药后等待太久才进食 * 运动量很大或在非习惯时间运动 * 运动前未检测血糖或未调整胰岛素剂量 * 饮酒 **预防低血糖** 预防低血糖总比不得不治疗它要好。随身携带速效糖源。 * 运动时，请检测您的血糖水平。确保随身携带零食。 * 与您的提供者讨论在运动日减少胰岛素剂量。 * 询问您的提供者是否需要睡前吃零食以预防夜间低血糖。蛋白质零食可能是最好的选择。 * 不要空腹饮酒。女性每天饮酒不应超过 1 杯，男性每天不应超过 2 杯。 家人和朋友应该知道如何提供帮助。他们应该知道： * 低血糖的症状以及如何判断您是否有这些症状。 * 他们应该给您吃多少以及什么样的食物。 * 何时呼叫紧急救援。 * 如何注射胰高血糖素（glucagon），这是一种可以升高血糖的激素。您的提供者会告诉您何时使用这种药物。 如果您患有糖尿病，请务必佩戴医疗警示手环或项链。这有助于急救人员知道您患有糖尿病。 **当您的血糖变低时** 每当您有低血糖症状时，请检测您的血糖。如果您的血糖低于 70 mg/dL，请立即进行自我治疗。 1. 吃含有约 15 克 (g) 碳水化合物的食物。例如： * 4 片葡萄糖片 * 半杯（4 盎司或 120 毫升）果汁或普通（非无糖）汽水 * 5 或 6 颗硬糖 * 1 汤匙 (tbsp) 或 15 毫升糖，干吃或溶于水中 * 1 汤匙 (15 毫升) 蜂蜜或糖浆 2. 等待约 15 分钟再进食。注意不要吃太多。这会导致高血糖和体重增加。 3. 再次检测您的血糖。 4. 如果 15 分钟后您感觉没有好转，且血糖仍低于 70 mg/dL (3.9 mmol/L)，请再吃一份含 15 克碳水化合物的零食。 如果您的血糖处于较安全的范围——超过 70 mg/dL (3.9 mmol/L)——但距离下一顿正餐还有一个多小时，您可能需要吃一份含有碳水化合物和蛋白质的零食。 询问您的提供者如何处理这种情况。如果这些升高血糖的步骤不起作用，请立即联系您的提供者。 **与您的医生或护士交谈** 如果您使用胰岛素且血糖频繁或持续偏低，请询问您的提供者或护士您是否： * 注射胰岛素的方法是否正确 * 需要不同类型的针头 * 应该改变胰岛素的用量 * 应该改变使用的胰岛素种类 在未先与您的提供者或护士交谈之前，请勿进行任何更改。 有时低血糖可能是由于误服了错误的药物造成的。请与您的药剂师核对您...

Back-Translation (to English):

Low Blood Sugar — Self-care Low blood sugar refers to the situation where your blood sugar (glucose) is lower than normal levels. Low blood sugar can happen in people who have diabetes and are taking insulin or other certain medicines to control diabetes. Low blood sugar can cause dangerous symptoms. Learn how to recognize the symptoms of low blood sugar and how to prevent them. **What is low blood sugar?** Low blood sugar is medically called hypoglycemia (Hypoglycemia). Blood sugar levels lower than 70 mg/dL (3.9 mmol/L) are considered low and may cause harm to you. Blood sugar levels lower than 54 mg/dL (3.0 mmol/L) require immediate action. If you have diabetes and are taking any one of the following diabetes medicines, you are at risk of developing low blood sugar: * Insulin (Insulin) * Glyburide (Micronase), Glipizide (Glucotrol), Glimepiride (Amaryl), Repaglinide (Prandin) or Nateglinide (Starlix) If you have had low blood sugar levels before, your risk of developing low blood sugar also increases. **Recognizing low blood sugar** Learn how to tell when your blood sugar becomes low. Symptoms include: * Weakness or feeling tired * Trembling * Sweating * Headache * Hunger * Feeling uneasy, nervous, or anxious * Grumpy * Unclear thinking * Double vision (diplopia) or blurred vision * Fast heartbeat or pounding heartbeat Sometimes, even if you do not have symptoms, your blood sugar may be too low. If blood sugar is too low, you might: * Faint * Have a seizure * Fall into a coma Some people who have had diabetes for a long time can no longer feel low blood sugar. This is called hypoglycemic unawareness. Please consult your healthcare provider whether wearing a continuous glucose monitor and sensor can help you detect when blood sugar is too low, thereby helping to prevent symptoms. **Check blood sugar often** Discuss with your provider when you should check your blood sugar every day. Item: EVAL_0148 | Document: RESP_001 | Model: Model C

Original English:

Asthma - quick-relief drugs Asthma quick-relief medicines work fast to control asthma symptoms. You take them when you are coughing, wheezing, having trouble breathing, or having an asthma attack. They are also called rescue medicines. Many of these medicines are called "bronchodilators" because they open (dilate) and help relax the muscles of your airways (bronchi). You and your health care provider can make a plan for the quick-relief medicines that work for you. This plan will include when you should take them and how much you should take. Plan ahead. Make sure you do not run out. Bring enough medicine with you when you travel. Short-acting Beta-agonists Short-acting beta-agonists are the most common quick-relief medicines for treating asthma attacks and are considered to be bronchodilators. They can be used just before exercising to help prevent asthma symptoms caused by exercise. They work by relaxing the muscles of your airways, and this lets you breathe better during an attack. Tell your provider if you are using quick-relief medicines twice a week or more to control your asthma symptoms. Your asthma may not be under control, and your provider may need to change your dose of daily control medicines. Some quick-relief asthma medicines include: Albuterol (ProAir HFA, Proventil HFA, Ventolin HFA) Levalbuterol (Xopenex HFA) Metaproterenol Terbutaline Short-acting beta-agonists may cause these side effects: Anxiety. Fast and irregular heartbeats. Call your provider right away if you have this side effect. Headache. Restlessness. Tremor (your hand or another part of your body may shake). Oral Steroids Your provider might prescribe oral steroids when you have an asthma attack that is not going away. These are medicines that you take by mouth as pills, capsules, or liquids. Oral steroids are not quick-relief medicines but are often given for 7 to 14 days when your symptoms flare-up. Oral steroids include: Methylprednisolone Prednisone Prednisolone

Translation (Chinese (Simplified)):

哮喘 - 速效药物 哮喘速效药物可以快速控制哮喘症状。你在咳嗽、喘鸣、呼吸困难或发生哮喘发作时服用这些药物。它们也被称为“急救药物”。 这些药物中有许多被称为“支气管扩张剂（bronchodilators）”，因为它们可以打开（扩张）并帮助放松你气道（支气管，bronchi）的肌肉。 你和你的医疗保健提供者可以一起制定一个适合你的速效药物用药计划。这个计划会包括你什么时候应该用药，以及你每次应该用多少药。 要提前做好计划。确保你的药不要用完。外出或旅行时要带足够的药物。 短效β受体激动剂（Short-acting Beta-agonists） 短效β受体激动剂是治疗哮喘发作最常用的速效药物，并被认为是支气管扩张剂。 它们可以在运动前使用，以帮助预防运动引起的哮喘症状。它们通过放松你气道的肌肉来起作用，这样在发作时你就能更好地呼吸。 如果你每周使用速效药物两次或更多次来控制哮喘症状，要告诉你的医疗保健提供者。你的哮喘可能没有得到良好控制，你的医疗保健提供者可能需要调整你每天使用的控制药物的剂量。 一些速效哮喘药物包括： Albuterol（沙丁胺醇，商品名：ProAir HFA、Proventil HFA、Ventolin HFA） Levalbuterol（左旋沙丁胺醇，商品名：Xopenex HFA） Metaproterenol（间羟舒喘灵） Terbutaline（特布他林） 短效β受体激动剂可能会引起以下副作用： 焦虑。 心跳加快且不规则。如果出现这种副作用，请立即联系你的医疗保健提供者。 头痛。 坐立不安。 震颤（你的手或身体的其他部位可能会发抖）。 口服类固醇（Oral Steroids） 当你出现难以缓解的哮喘发作时，你的医疗保健提供者可能会给你开口服类固醇。这些药物是以药片、胶囊或液体的形式口服的。 口服类固醇不是速效药物，但在症状加重时，通常会连续使用 7 到 14 天。 口服类固醇包括： Methylprednisolone（甲泼尼龙） Prednisone（泼尼松） Prednisolone（泼尼松龙）

Asthma - Quick-relief Medications Asthma quick-relief medications can quickly control asthma symptoms. You take these medications when you are coughing, wheezing, having difficulty breathing, or having an asthma attack. They are also called “rescue medications.” Many of these medications are called “bronchodilators” because they can open (dilate) and help relax the muscles of your airways (bronchi). You and your healthcare provider can work together to develop a quick-relief medication plan that suits you. This plan will include when you should take the medication and how much you should take each time. Plan ahead. Make sure you do not run out of your medication. Take enough medication with you when going out or traveling. Short-acting Beta-agonists Short-acting beta-agonists are the most commonly used quick-relief medications for treating asthma attacks and are considered bronchodilators. They can be used before exercise to help prevent exercise-induced asthma symptoms. They work by relaxing the muscles of your airways so that you can breathe better during an attack. If you use quick-relief medication two or more times a week to control asthma symptoms, tell your healthcare provider. Your asthma may not be well controlled, and your healthcare provider may need to adjust the dose of the controller medication you use every day. Some quick-relief asthma medications include: Albuterol (brand names: ProAir HFA, Proventil HFA, Ventolin HFA) Levalbuterol (brand name: Xopenex HFA) Metaproterenol Terbutaline Short-acting beta-agonists may cause the following side effects: Anxiety. Fast and irregular heartbeat. If this side effect occurs, contact your healthcare provider right away. Headache. Restlessness. Tremor (your hands or other parts of your body may shake). 哮喘 —— 快速缓解药物 哮喘快速缓解药物能迅速控制哮喘症状。当您出现咳嗽、喘息、呼吸困难或哮喘发作时，请服用这些药物。它们也被称为急救药物。 许多这类药物被称为“支气管扩张剂”，因为它们能打开（扩张）并帮助放松气道（支气管）的肌肉。 您和您的医疗服务提供者可以制定一个适合您的快速缓解药物计划。该计划将包括您应该何时服药以及服用多少。 提前计划。确保药物不要用完。旅行时请随身携带足够的药物。 ### 短效 β-受体激动剂 短效 β-受体激动剂是治疗哮喘发作最常见的快速缓解药物，被归类为支气管扩张剂。 它们可以在运动前使用，以帮助预防由运动引起的哮喘症状。它们的作用是放松气道的肌肉，这能让您在发作期间呼吸更顺畅。 如果您每周使用两次或更多次快速缓解药物来控制哮喘症状，请告诉您的医疗服务提供者。您的哮喘可能没有得到控制，您的医疗服务提供者可能需要更改您的日常控制药物剂量。 一些快速缓解哮喘药物包括： * 沙丁胺醇 / Albuterol (ProAir HFA, Proventil HFA, Ventolin HFA) * 左沙丁胺醇 / Levalbuterol (Xopenex HFA) * 麦他特罗 / Metaproterenol * 特布他林 / Terbutaline 短效 β-受体激动剂可能会引起以下副作用： * 焦虑。 * 心跳过快和不规律。如果出现这种副作用，请立即致电您的医疗服务提供者。 * 头痛。 * 烦躁不安。 * 震颤（您的手或身体其他部位可能会发抖）。 ### 口服类固醇 当您的哮喘发作且没有好转时，您的医疗服务提供者可能会开具口服类固醇。这些是您通过口服服用的药物，形式为药片、胶囊或药液。 口服类固醇不是快速缓解药物，但在症状突然加重时，通常会开具 7 到 14 天的药量。 口服类固醇包括： * 甲泼尼龙 / Methylprednisolone * 泼尼松 / Prednisone * 泼尼松龙 / Prednisolone

Asthma — Quick-Relief Medicines Asthma quick-relief medicines can rapidly control asthma symptoms. Please take these medicines when you have coughing, wheezing, difficulty breathing, or an asthma attack. They are also called rescue medicines. Many of these medicines are called "bronchodilators" because they can open (dilate) and help relax the muscles of the airways (bronchi). You and your healthcare provider can develop a quick-relief medicine plan that works for you. The plan will include when you should take the medicine and how much to take. Plan ahead. Make sure not to run out of medicine. Please carry enough medicine with you when traveling. ### Short-acting Beta-agonists Short-acting beta-agonists are the most common quick-relief medicines for treating asthma attacks and are classified as bronchodilators. They can be used before exercise to help prevent asthma symptoms caused by exercise. They work by relaxing the muscles of the airways, which allows you to breathe more easily during an attack. Tell your healthcare provider if you use quick-relief medicines twice or more a week to control asthma symptoms. Your asthma may not be under control, and your healthcare provider may need to change your daily control medicine dosage. Some quick-relief asthma medicines include: * Albuterol (ProAir HFA, Proventil HFA, Ventolin HFA) * Levalbuterol (Xopenex HFA) * Metaproterenol * Terbutaline Short-acting beta-agonists may cause the following side effects: * Anxiety. * Fast and irregular heartbeat. If this side effect occurs, please call your healthcare provider immediately. * Headache. * Restlessness. * Tremors (your hands or other parts of your body may shake). ### Oral Steroids Your healthcare provider may prescribe oral steroids when your asthma attacks and does not get better. These are medicines you take by mouth, in the form of tablets, capsules, or liquid. Oral steroids are not quick-relief medicines, but when symptoms suddenly worse...

Item: EVAL_0196 | Document: MED_001 | Model: Model C

Original English:

ACE inhibitors Angiotensin-converting enzyme (ACE) inhibitors are medicines. They treat heart, blood vessel, and kidney problems. How ACE inhibitors help ACE inhibitors are used to treat heart disease and high blood pressure. These medicines make your heart work less hard by lowering your blood pressure. This keeps some kinds of heart disease from getting worse. Most people who have heart failure take one of these medicines or similar medicines. These medicines treat high blood pressure, strokes, or heart attacks. They may help lower your risk for stroke or heart attack. They are also used to treat kidney problems. This can help keep your kidneys from getting worse or even improve the function of your kidneys, especially if you have diabetes. If you have these problems, ask your health care provider if you should be taking these medicines. Types of ACE inhibitors There are many different names and brands of ACE inhibitors. Most work as well as another. Side effects may be different for different ones. Taking Your ACE inhibitors ACE inhibitors are pills that you take by mouth. Take all of your medicines as your provider told you to. Follow up with your provider regularly. Your provider will check your blood pressure and do blood tests to make sure the medicines are working properly. Your provider may change your dose from time to time. In addition: Try to take your medicines at the same time each day. Don't stop taking your medicines without talking to your provider first. Plan ahead so that you do not run out of medicine. Make sure you have enough with you when you travel. Before taking ibuprofen (Advil, Motrin) or aspirin, talk to your provider. Tell your provider what other medicines you are taking, including anything you bought without a prescription, diuretics (water pills), potassium pills, or herbal or dietary supplements. Don't take ACE inhibitors if you are planning to become pregnant, are pregnant, or are breastfeeding. Contact your provider promptly...

ACE Inhibitors Angiotensin-converting enzyme (ACE) inhibitors are a class of medicines. They are used to treat problems of the heart, blood vessels, and kidneys. Effects of ACE inhibitors ACE inhibitors are used to treat heart disease and high blood pressure. These medicines lower blood pressure so that the heart does not have to work as hard. This can prevent certain types of heart disease from getting worse. Most people with heart failure take this type of medicine or a similar medicine. These medicines are used to treat high blood pressure, stroke, or heart attack. They may help reduce the risk of stroke or heart attack. They are also used to treat kidney problems. This can help prevent kidney function from getting worse, and even improve kidney function, especially if you have diabetes. If you have these problems, ask your healthcare provider whether you should take these medicines. Types of ACE inhibitors There are many different names and brands of ACE inhibitors. Most medicines have similar effectiveness. But the side effects of different medicines may be different. Taking your ACE inhibitor ACE inhibitors are oral tablets. Take all medicines as directed by your healthcare provider. Follow up with your healthcare provider regularly. Your healthcare provider will check your blood pressure and do blood tests to make sure the medicine is working and is safe to use. Your healthcare provider may adjust your dose from time to time. In addition: Try to take your medicine at the same time every day. Do not stop taking your medicine without first talking with your healthcare provider. Plan ahead to avoid running out of medicine. Make sure you carry enough medicine with you when you travel. Talk with your healthcare provider before taking ibuprofen (brand names Advil, Motrin) or aspirin. Tell your healthcare provider about other medicines you are taking, including any over-the-counter medicines, diuretics (water pills), potassium tablets, or herbal...

Original English:

ACE inhibitors Angiotensin-converting enzyme (ACE) inhibitors are medicines. They treat heart, blood vessel, and kidney problems. How ACE inhibitors help ACE inhibitors are used to treat heart disease and high blood pressure. These medicines make your heart work less hard by lowering your blood pressure. This keeps some kinds of heart disease from getting worse. Most people who have heart failure take one of these medicines or similar medicines. These medicines treat high blood pressure, strokes, or heart attacks. They may help lower your risk for stroke or heart attack. They are also used to treat kidney problems. This can help keep your kidneys from getting worse or even improve the function of your kidneys, especially if you have diabetes. If you have these problems, ask your health care provider if you should be taking these medicines. Types of ACE inhibitors There are many different names and brands of ACE inhibitors. Most work as well as another. Side effects may be different for different ones. Taking Your ACE inhibitors ACE inhibitors are pills that you take by mouth. Take all of your medicines as your provider told you to. Follow up with your provider regularly. Your provider will check your blood pressure and do blood tests to make sure the medicines are working properly. Your provider may change your dose from time to time. In addition: Try to take your medicines at the same time each day. Don't stop taking your medicines without talking to your provider first. Plan ahead so that you do not run out of medicine. Make sure you have enough with you when you travel. Before taking ibuprofen (Advil, Motrin) or aspirin, talk to your provider. Tell your provider what other medicines you are taking, including anything you bought without a prescription, diuretics (water pills), potassium pills, or herbal or dietary supplements. Don't take ACE inhibitors if you are planning to become pregnant, are pregnant, or are breastfeeding. Contact your provider promptly...

Item: EVAL_0220 | Document: EMER_001 | Model: Model C

Original English:

Stroke - discharge You were in the hospital after having a stroke. A stroke happens when blood flow to part of the brain stops. At home follow your health care provider's instructions on self-care. Use the information below as a reminder. When You're in the Hospital First, you received treatment to prevent further damage to the brain, and to help the heart, lungs, and other important organs heal. After you were stable, your providers did testing and started treatment to help you recover from the stroke and prevent a future stroke. You may have stayed in a special unit that helps people recover after a stroke. What to Expect at Home Because of possible injury to the brain from the stroke, you may notice problems with: Changes in behavior Doing easy tasks Memory Moving one side of the body Muscle spasms Paying attention Sensation or awareness of one part of the body Swallowing Talking or understanding others Thinking Seeing to one side (hemianopsia) You may need help with daily activities you used to do alone before the stroke. You may have physical or occupational therapy to restore your ability to perform these functions. Depression after a stroke is fairly common as you learn to live with the changes. It may develop soon after the stroke or up to 2 years after the stroke. Do not drive your car without your provider's permission. Moving Around Moving around and doing normal tasks may be hard after a stroke. Make sure your home is safe. Ask your provider, therapist, or nurse about making changes in your home to make it easier to do everyday activities. Find out about what you can do to prevent falls and keep your bathroom safe to use. Stroke - discharge You were in the hospital after having a stroke. A stroke happens when blood flow to part of the brain stops. At home follow your health care provider's instructions on self-care. Stroke - Discharge Instructions You were hospitalized for a stroke. A stroke is when blood flow to part of the brain is interrupted. Please follow the self-care instructions from your healthcare provider after discharge. The following information is for your reference. During Your Hospital Stay First, you received treatment to prevent further damage to the brain and help the heart, lungs, and other vital organs recover. After your condition stabilized, healthcare providers performed examinations and began treatment to help you recover from the stroke and prevent it from happening again. You may have received treatment in a specialized unit that helps stroke patients recover. What to Expect After Discharge Because a stroke can cause damage to the brain, you may notice the following problems: Behavioral changes Difficulty completing simple tasks Memory problems Difficulty moving one side of the body Muscle spasms Attention problems Sensation or awareness problems in parts of the body Difficulty swallowing Difficulty speaking or understanding others Thinking problems Loss of vision on one side (hemianopia) You may need help from others to complete daily activities you could previously do independently. You may need physical therapy or occupational therapy to regain these functions. Depression after stroke is relatively common and is a normal response as you adjust to life changes. Depression may occur shortly after a stroke or may occur within 2 years after the stroke. Do not drive a car without permission from your healthcare provider. Activity After a stroke, moving around and completing daily tasks may become difficult. Make sure your home environment is safe. Ask your healthcare provider, therapist, or nurse about how to modify your home environment to make daily activities more convenient. Learn how to prevent falls and how to ensure bathroom safety. 中风 - 出院 您因中风住院治疗。当流向大脑某一部分的血液停止时，就会发生中风。 回家后，请遵照医务人员的指示进行自我护理。以下信息可作为提醒。 **住院期间** 首先，您接受了治疗以防止大脑受到进一步损伤，并帮助心脏、肺部和其他重要器官康复。 待病情稳定后，医务人员为您进行了检查并开始治疗，以帮助您从中风中康复并预防再次中风。您可能曾住在专门帮助中风患者康复的特殊病房。 **回家后的预期情况** 由于中风可能对大脑造成损伤，您可能会注意到以下方面的问题： * 行为改变 * 做简单的任务 * 记忆力 * 移动身体的一侧 * 肌肉痉挛 * 注意力 * 身体某部位的感觉或知觉 * 吞咽 * 说话或理解他人 * 思考 * 单侧视力（偏盲） 您可能需要他人协助完成中风前能独自进行的日常活动。您可能需要接受物理治疗或职业治疗，以恢复执行这些功能的能力。 随着您学习适应这些变化，中风后出现抑郁症是相当常见的。它可能在中风后不久出现，也可能在中风后长达 2 年内出现。 未经医务人员许可，请勿开车。 **活动与行动** 中风后，四处走动和做日常事务可能会很困难。 确保您的居家环境安全。向您的医务人员、治疗师或护士咨询如何改造家居环境，以便更轻松地进行日常活动。 了解您可以采取哪些措施来预防跌倒，并确保浴室使用安全。 家人和看护者可能需要在以下方面提供帮助： * 进行锻炼以保持手肘、肩膀和其他关节灵活 * 观察关节是否僵硬（挛缩） * 确保正确使用夹板 * 确保坐着或躺着时手臂和腿部处于良好的位置 如果您或您的亲人使用轮椅，复诊检查轮椅是否合适非常重要，以防止皮肤溃疡。 * 每天检查脚后跟、脚踝、膝盖、臀部、尾骨和手肘是否有压疮。 * 白天坐在轮椅上时，每小时变换几次姿势，以预防压疮。 * 如果您有痉挛问题，请了解是什么原因导致其恶化。您或您的看护者可以学习锻炼方法来保持肌肉放松。 * 学习如何预防压疮。 **思考与说话** 让穿脱衣服更容易的技巧包括： * 魔术贴比纽扣和拉链容易得多。所有的纽扣和拉链都应位于衣服的正面。 * 穿套头衫和一脚蹬（无需系带）的鞋子。 中风患者可能会有言语或语言问题。您可能已被转介给言语治疗师来帮助解决这些问题。给家人和看护者改善沟通的建议包括： * 减少干扰和噪音。放低声音。移步到较安静的房间。不要大喊大叫。 * 留出充足的时间让患者回答问题和理解指令。中风后，处理听到的话需要更长的时间。 * 使用简单的词语和句子，语速要慢。提问方式要让患者能用“是”或“否”来回答。尽可能给出明确的选择。不要给出太多的选项。 * 将指令分解成细小且简单的步骤。 * 如有需要请重复。使用熟悉的名字和地点。在转换话题时要提前告知。 * 如果可能，在接触或说话前先进行眼神交流。 * 尽可能使用道具或视觉提示。不要给出太多的选项。您可以使用指点、手势或绘画。使用平板电脑或手机等电子设备展示图片，以辅助沟通。 **肠道护理** 帮助肠道顺畅运作的神经可能会在中风后受损。建立一套常规。一旦找到有效的排便规律，就要坚持下去： * 选定一个固定的时间，例如饭后或温水浴后，尝试排便。 * 要有耐心。排便可能需要 15 到 45 分钟。 * 尝试轻轻按摩腹部，帮助粪便在结肠中移动。 避免便秘： * 多喝流质饮品。 * 尽可能保持活跃或增加活动量。 * 吃富含纤维的食物。 * 询问医务人员您正在服用的药物是否会引起便秘（例如治疗抑郁症、疼痛、膀胱控制和肌肉痉挛的药物）。 **服药提示** 回家前配好所有处方药。严格按照医务人员的指示服药非常重要。在未咨询医务人员之前，请勿服用任何其他药物、补充剂、维生素或草药。 您可能会被开具以下一种或多种药物。这些药物旨在调节您的血压或胆固醇，并防止血液凝固。它们可能有助于预防再次中风： * 抗血小板药物（阿司匹林或氯吡格雷）有助于防止血液凝固。 * 血液稀释剂，如华法林或新型口服抗凝药（NOACs，如阿哌沙班、利伐沙班等）。 * 钙通道阻滞剂、利尿剂（排水丸）和 ACE 抑制剂药物可调节血压并保护心脏。 * 他汀类药物可降低胆固醇。 * 如果您患有糖尿病，请将血糖控制在医务人员建议的水平。 请勿停止服用任何这些药物。 某些血液稀释剂，如华法林（Coumadin），需要您进行额外的血液检查。 **保持健康** 如果您有吞咽困难，必须学习遵循特殊的饮食习惯，以确保进食更安全。吞咽问题的迹象是进食时噎住或咳嗽。学习让进食和吞咽更轻松、更安全的技巧。 避免咸味和油腻的食物，少去快餐店，以使您的心脏和血管...

Stroke - Discharge You were hospitalized for treatment due to a stroke. A stroke occurs when blood flow to a certain part of the brain stops. After returning home, please follow the medical staff's instructions for self-care. The following information can serve as a reminder. **During the hospital stay** First, you received treatment to prevent further damage to the brain, and to help the heart, lungs, and other vital organs recover. After your condition stabilized, medical staff performed examinations for you and started treatment to help you recover from the stroke and prevent another stroke. You may have stayed in a special ward dedicated to helping stroke patients recover. **What to expect after returning home** Since a stroke may cause damage to the brain, you may notice problems in the following areas: * Behavior changes * Doing simple tasks * Memory * Moving one side of the body * Muscle spasms * Attention * Sensation or perception in a certain part of the body * Swallowing * Speaking or understanding others * Thinking * Vision on one side (hemianopia) You may need assistance from others to complete daily activities that you could perform alone before the stroke. You may need to receive physical therapy or occupational therapy to restore the ability to perform these functions. As you learn to adapt to these changes, the appearance of depression after a stroke is quite common. It may appear shortly after the stroke, or it may appear up to 2 years after the stroke. Do not drive without permission from medical staff. **Activity and Mobility** After a stroke, moving around and doing daily chores may be difficult. Ensure your home environment is safe. Consult your medical staff, therapist, or nurse on how to modify the home environment to perform daily activities more easily. Item: EVAL_0244 | Document: SURG_001 | Model: Model C

Original English:

Surgical wound care - open An incision is a cut through the skin that is made during surgery. It is also called a surgical wound. Some incisions are small, others are long. The size of the incision depends on the kind of surgery you had. Sometimes, an incision breaks open. This may happen along the entire cut or just part of it. Your surgeon may decide not to close it again with sutures (stitches). What to Expect at Home If your surgeon does not close your wound again with sutures, you need to care for it at home, since it may take time to heal. The wound will heal from the bottom to the top. A dressing helps absorb drainage and keep the skin from closing before the wound underneath fills in. Proper Handwashing It is important to clean your hands before you change your dressing. You can use an alcohol-based cleanser. Or, you can wash your hands using these steps: Take all jewelry off your hands. Wet your hands, pointing them downward under warm running water. Add soap and wash your hands for 15 to 30 seconds (sing "Happy Birthday" or the "Alphabet Song" one time through). Clean under your nails also. Rinse well. Dry with a clean towel. Removing the Old Dressing Your health care provider will tell you how often to change your dressing. To prepare for the dressing change: Clean your hands before touching the dressing. Make sure you have all the supplies handy. Have a clean work surface. Remove the old dressing: Carefully loosen the tape from your skin. Use a clean (not sterile) medical glove to grab the old dressing and pull it off. If the dressing sticks to the wound, wet it and try again, unless your provider instructed you to pull it off dry. Put the old dressing in a plastic bag and set it aside. Clean your hands again after you take off the old dressing. Caring for the Wound You may use a gauze pad or soft cloth to clean the skin around your wound: Use a normal saline solution (salt water) or mild soapy water. Soak the gauze or cloth in the saline solutio...

Translation (Chinese (Simplified)):

手术伤口护理 - 开放性伤口 切口是手术时在皮肤上做的切开口子，也叫手术伤口。有的切口很小，有的比较长。切口的大小取决于您所做的手术类型。 有时，切口会裂开。这可能发生在整个切口上，也可能只是在一部分。您的外科医生可能会决定不再用缝线（针线）把它重新缝合。 在家中可以预期的情况 如果您的外科医生没有再次用缝线把伤口缝合，您需要在家中照顾伤口，因为它可能需要一段时间才能愈合。伤口会从底部向上愈合。敷料可以帮助吸收渗出物，并防止表面皮肤在下面的伤口尚未填满前就先闭合。 正确的洗手方法 在更换敷料前，清洁双手非常重要。您可以使用含酒精的洗手液。或者，您可以按照以下步骤用水和肥皂洗手： 1. 取下手上的所有首饰。 2. 在温水流下把手弄湿，手指朝下。 3. 加入肥皂，搓洗双手 15 到 30 秒（可以在心里唱一遍“生日快乐歌”或“字母歌”）。同时清洁指甲缝。 4. 彻底冲洗干净。 5. 用干净的毛巾擦干。 去除旧敷料 您的医疗服务提供者会告诉您需要多长时间更换一次敷料。为更换敷料做准备时： - 在接触敷料前先洗手。 - 确保所有用品都在手边。 - 准备一个干净的操作台面。 去除旧敷料： - 小心地将胶带从皮肤上慢慢撕开。 - 戴上干净的（非无菌）医用手套，抓住旧敷料并将其取下。 - 如果敷料粘在伤口上，可先把敷料弄湿再试一次，除非您的医生特别要求您在干的情况下直接撕下。 - 把旧敷料放入塑料袋中，先放在一旁。 - 取下旧敷料后，再次洗手。 伤口护理 您可以用纱布垫或柔软的布清洁伤口周围的皮肤： - 使用生理盐水（盐水）或温和的肥皂水。 - 将纱布或布浸泡在生理盐水或肥皂水中，轻轻点按或擦拭皮肤。 - 尽量清除所有渗出物以及皮肤上积累的干血或其他污物。 - 不要使用皮肤清洁剂、酒精、双氧水（过氧化氢）、碘酒或含抗菌成分的肥皂。这些会损伤伤口组织并减慢愈合。 您的医生可能还会让您冲洗伤口： - 用注射器吸满盐水或肥皂水，以医生推荐的为准。 - 将注射器与伤口保持 1 到 6 英寸（2.5 到 15 厘米）的距离。用足够的力度将液体冲入伤口，以冲掉渗出物和分泌物。 - 用干净、柔软、干燥的布或纱布轻轻拍干伤口。 - 除非医生说可以，否则不要在伤口上或伤口周围涂抹任何乳液、药膏、面霜或草药制品。 敷上新敷料 按照医生教给您的方法，将干净的敷料覆盖在伤口上。您可能在使用“湿敷-干敷”敷料，这种敷料需要在敷上前先弄湿。 完成后请洗手。 将旧敷料和其他用过的用品放入防水塑料袋中。把袋口扎紧，再套一个袋子封好，然后丢入垃圾桶。 将因更换敷料而弄脏的衣物单独清洗，不要和其他衣物一起洗。询问医生是否需要在洗涤水中加入漂白剂。 每片敷料只能使用一次。绝不要重复使用。 何时联系医生 如果出现以下情况，请联系您的医生： - 伤口部位的发红、疼痛、肿胀或出血增多。 - 伤口变大或变深，或者看起来干枯、发黑。 - 从伤口内或周围流出的渗出物增多，或变得浓稠、棕褐色、绿色或黄色，或有恶臭（提示有脓）。 - 体温达到或超过 100.5°F（38°C）。

Back-Translation (to English):

Surgical Wound Care – Open Wounds An incision is a cut made in the skin during surgery, also called a surgical wound. Some incisions are very small, and some are relatively long. The size of the incision depends on the type of surgery you have had. Sometimes, the incision may split open. This may happen along the entire incision, or only in a part of it. Your surgeon may decide not to use stitches (needle and thread) to sew it closed again. What to expect at home If your surgeon has not stitched the wound closed again, you will need to care for the wound at home, because it may take some time to heal. The wound will heal from the bottom up. Dressings can help absorb drainage and prevent the surface skin from closing before the wound underneath has filled in. Proper handwashing It is very important to clean your hands before changing the dressing. You can use an alcohol-based hand sanitizer. Or, you can wash your hands with water and soap by following these steps: 1. Remove all jewelry from your hands. 2. Wet your hands under running warm water, with your fingers pointing down. 3. Add soap and rub your hands together for 15 to 30 seconds (you can silently sing “Happy Birthday” or the “Alphabet Song” once). Clean under your fingernails at the same time. 4. Rinse thoroughly. 5. Dry with a clean towel. Removing the old dressing Your health care provider will tell you how often you need to change the dressing. When preparing to change the dressing: - Wash your hands before touching the dressing. - Make sure all supplies are within reach. - Prepare a clean work surface. To remove the old dressing: - Carefully and slowly peel the tape away from the skin. - Put on clean (non-sterile) medical gloves, grasp the old dressing, and remove it. - If the dressing sticks to the wound, moisten the dressing first and then try again, unless your doctor has specifically asked you to pull it off dry. - Place the old dressing into a plastic bag and set it ...

Translation (Chinese (Simplified)):

手术伤口护理 - 开放性伤口 切口是手术过程中在皮肤上做的切开。它也被称为手术伤口。有些切口很小，有些则很长。切口的大小取决于您接受的手术类型。 有时，切口会裂开。这可能发生在整个切口处，也可能只是部分裂开。您的外科医生可能会决定不再用缝线（缝合）将其闭合。 居家护理须知 如果您的外科医生不再用缝线闭合您的伤口，您需要在家护理伤口，因为愈合可能需要时间。伤口会从底部向顶部愈合。敷料有助于吸收渗液，并防止在下方伤口填充之前皮肤过早闭合。 正确洗手 在更换敷料之前清洁双手非常重要。您可以使用含酒精的清洁剂。或者，您可以按以下步骤洗手： 取下手上所有的首饰。 将双手指向下方，在温热的流动水下打湿。 加入肥皂，洗手15至30秒（唱一遍"生日快乐歌"或"字母歌"）。同时清洁指甲下方。 彻底冲洗干净。 用干净的毛巾擦干。 取下旧敷料 您的医疗保健提供者会告诉您多久更换一次敷料。准备更换敷料时： 在触摸敷料之前清洁双手。 确保所有用品都准备好并放在手边。 准备一个清洁的工作台面。 取下旧敷料： 小心地将胶带从皮肤上松开。 戴上清洁（非无菌）的医用手套，抓住旧敷料并将其取下。 如果敷料粘在伤口上，请将其弄湿后再试，除非您的医疗提供者指示您干取敷料。 将旧敷料放入塑料袋中并放在一边。 取下旧敷料后再次清洁双手。 伤口护理 您可以使用纱布垫或软布清洁伤口周围的皮肤： 使用生理盐水（盐水）或温和的肥皂水。 将纱布或布浸入盐水或肥皂水中，轻轻擦拭皮肤。 尽量清除所有渗液以及可能积聚在皮肤上的干血或其他物质。 不要使用皮肤清洁剂、酒精、过氧化氢、碘或含有抗菌化学物质的肥皂。这些会损伤伤口组织并减缓愈合。 您的医疗提供者也可能要求您冲洗伤口： 用盐水或肥皂水填充注射器，具体使用哪种请遵循医疗提供者的建议。 将注射器保持在距离伤口1至6英寸（2.5至15厘米）的位置。用足够的力度向伤口内喷射，以冲洗掉渗液和分泌物。 用干净、柔软、干燥的布或纱布轻轻拍干伤口。 除非您的医疗提供者表示可以，否则不要在伤口上或周围涂抹任何乳液、药膏或草药制剂。 敷上新敷料 按照您的医疗提供者教您的方法将清洁的敷料敷在伤口上。您可能使用的是湿-干敷料，需要在敷用前将敷料弄湿。 完成后清洁双手。 将旧敷料和其他用过的用品丢入防水塑料袋中。将袋子紧紧封好，然后双层包装后再丢入垃圾桶。 更换敷料时弄脏的衣物要与其他衣物分开清洗。请咨询您的医疗提供者是否需要在洗涤水中加入漂白剂。 敷料只能使用一次。切勿重复使用。 何时联系医生 如果出现以下情况，请联系您的医疗提供者： 伤口部位出现更多发红、疼痛、肿胀或出血。 伤口变大或变深，或看起来干燥或发黑。 伤口处或周围的渗液增加或变得浓稠、呈棕褐色、绿色或黄色，或有异味（这表明有脓液）。 您的体温达到100.5°F（38°C）或更高。

Back-Translation (to English):

Surgical Wound Care - Open Wound An incision is a cut made in the skin during a surgical procedure. It is also called a surgical wound. Some incisions are small, while others are long. The size of the incision depends on the type of surgery you are having. Sometimes, an incision will open up. This may happen along the entire incision, or only part of it may open. Your surgeon may decide not to close it again with stitches (sutures). What to Know About Home Care If your surgeon does not close your wound again with stitches, you will need to care for the wound at home because healing may take time. The wound will heal from the bottom up. Dressings help absorb drainage and prevent the skin from closing too early before the wound underneath has filled in. Proper Hand Washing It is very important to clean your hands before changing the dressing. You can use an alcohol-based cleanser. Or, you can wash your hands as follows: Remove all jewelry from your hands. Point your hands downward and wet them under warm running water. If the dressing sticks to the wound, wet it and try again, unless your healthcare provider instructs you to remove the dressing dry. Place the old dressing in a plastic bag and set it aside.
