Original English:

Surgical wound care - open An incision is a cut through the skin that is made during surgery. It is also called a surgical wound. Some incisions are small, others are long. The size of the incision depends on the kind of surgery you had. Sometimes, an incision breaks open. This may happen along the entire cut or just part of it. Your surgeon may decide not to close it again with sutures (stitches). What to Expect at Home If your surgeon does not close your wound again with sutures, you need to care for it at home, since it may take time to heal. The wound will heal from the bottom to the top. A dressing helps absorb drainage and keep the skin from closing before the wound underneath fills in. Proper Handwashing It is important to clean your hands before you change your dressing. You can use an alcohol-based cleanser. Or, you can wash your hands using these steps: Take all jewelry off your hands. Wet your hands, pointing them downward under warm running water. Add soap and wash your hands for 15 to 30 seconds (sing "Happy Birthday" or the "Alphabet Song" one time through). Clean under your nails also. Rinse well. Dry with a clean towel. Removing the Old Dressing Your health care provider will tell you how often to change your dressing. To prepare for the dressing change: Clean your hands before touching the dressing. Make sure you have all the supplies handy. Have a clean work surface. Remove the old dressing: Carefully loosen the tape from your skin. Use a clean (not sterile) medical glove to grab the old dressing and pull it off. If the dressing sticks to the wound, wet it and try again, unless your provider instructed you to pull it off dry. Put the old dressing in a plastic bag and set it aside. Clean your hands again after you take off the old dressing. Translation (Chinese (Simplified)):

手术伤口护理——开放性伤口 切口是手术过程中在皮肤上进行的割痕，也称为手术伤口。有些切口很小，有些则很长。切口的大小取决于您接受的手术类型。 有时，切口会裂开。这可能发生在整个切口或仅一部分。您的外科医生可能会决定不再用缝线（缝合线）将其重新缝合。 回家后的注意事项 如果您的外科医生没有用缝线再次缝合您的伤口，您需要在家进行护理，因为伤口愈合可能需要时间。伤口将从底部向上愈合。敷料有助于吸收引流液，并防止皮肤在伤口内部长好之前闭合。 正确的洗手方法 在更换敷料之前清洁双手非常重要。您可以使用含酒精的免洗洗手液。或者，您可以按照以下步骤洗手： * 摘下手上的所有首饰。 * 用温流动水打湿双手，手指向下。 * 涂上肥皂并搓洗双手15到30秒（唱一遍“生日快乐歌”或“字母歌”）。也要清洁指甲缝隙。 * 冲洗干净。 * 用干净的毛巾擦干。 移除旧敷料 您的医疗保健提供者会告诉您多久更换一次敷料。准备更换敷料时： * 触摸敷料前先清洁双手。 * 确保所有用品都在手边。 * 准备一个干净的操作台面。 * 移除旧敷料： * 小心地从皮肤上松开胶带。 * 使用干净（无需无菌）的医用手套抓住旧敷料并将其取下。 * 如果敷料粘在伤口上，请将其弄湿后再试，除非您的提供者指示您干着撕下。 * 将旧敷料放入塑料袋中并放在一旁。 * 取下旧敷料后再次清洁双手。 伤口护理 您可以使用纱布垫或软布清洁伤口周围的皮肤： * 使用生理盐水（盐水）或温和的肥皂水。 * 将纱布或布浸泡在盐水或肥皂水中，然后轻轻拍打或擦拭皮肤。 * 尽量清除所有积聚在皮肤上的引流液、干血或其他物质。 * **不要**使用皮肤清洁剂、酒精、双氧水、碘酒或含有抗菌化学成分的肥皂。这些会损伤伤口组织并减缓愈合。 您的提供者也可能要求您冲洗伤口： * 在注射器中装入盐水或肥皂水，具体取决于提供者的建议。 * 手持注射器，距离伤口1到6英寸（2.5到15厘米）。用力喷入伤口，以冲洗掉引流液和分泌物。 * 使用干净、柔软的干布或纱布小心地将伤口拍干。 * 不要在伤口上或周围涂抹任何乳液、药膏或草药，除非您的提供者说可以。 敷上新敷料 按照提供者教您的方法将干净的敷料敷在伤口上。您可能使用的是“湿转干”敷料，这种敷料在敷用前需要弄湿。 完成后清洁双手。 将旧敷料和其他用过的物品扔进防水塑料袋中。封紧袋口，然后再套一个袋子（双层包装），最后放入垃圾桶。 将更换敷料时弄脏的衣物与其他衣物分开清洗。询问您的提供者是否需要在洗涤水中加入漂白剂。 敷料只能使用一次。切勿重复使用。 何时联系医生 如果出现以下情况，请联系您的提供者： * 伤口部位的红肿、疼痛、肿胀或出血加重。 * 伤口变大或变深，或者看起来变干或发黑。 * 伤口流出或周围的引流液增加，或者变得浓稠、呈棕褐色、绿色或黄色，或有恶臭（这表明有脓液）。 * 您的体温达到 100.5°F (38°C) 或更高。

Item: EVAL_0268 | Document: SURG_002 | Model: Model C

Original English:

Hip replacement - discharge You had surgery to replace all or part of your hip joint with an artificial joint called a prosthesis. This article tells you what you need to do to care for your new hip when you leave the hospital. When You're in the Hospital You had a hip joint replacement surgery to replace all or part of your hip joint with an artificial joint. This artificial joint is called a prosthesis. What to Expect at Home By the time you go home, you should be able to walk with a walker or crutches without needing much help. Most people do not need them after 2 to 4 weeks. Check with your surgeon about when to stop using crutches. You should also be able to dress yourself with only a little help and be able to get into and out of your bed or a chair by yourself. You should also be able to use the toilet without much help. You will need to be careful that you do not dislocate your artificial hip, especially in the first few months after surgery. You will need to learn exercises that make your new hip stronger and take special precautions. You will need to have someone with you at home for 1 to 2 weeks after you leave the hospital or rehab center. You will need help preparing meals, bathing, moving around the house, and doing other daily activities. Over time, you should be able to return to your former level of activity. You will need to avoid some sports, such as downhill skiing or contact sports like football and soccer. But you should be able to do low impact activities, such as hiking, gardening, swimming, playing tennis, and golfing. Home Setup Your bed should be low enough for your feet to touch the floor when you sit on the edge of the bed. Your bed should also be high enough so that your hips are higher than your knees when you sit on the edge. You may not need a hospital bed, but your mattress should be firm. Keep tripping hazards out of your home. Learn to prevent falls. Remove loose wires or cords from areas you walk through to get from one...

Translation (Chinese (Simplified)):

--- 髋关节置换术 - 出院指导 您接受了手术，将全部或部分髋关节用一种叫做假体的人工关节替换。本资料将告诉您出院回家后如何护理您的新髋关节。 在医院期间 您做的是髋关节置换手术，用人工关节替换了全部或部分髋关节。这种人工关节叫做假体（prosthesis）。 回家后会怎样 当您出院回家时，您应该已经可以用助行器或拐杖行走，而且不需要太多帮助。大多数人在 2 到 4 周后就不再需要这些辅助工具。请咨询您的外科医生何时可以停止使用拐杖。 您还应该基本能自己穿衣，只需要少量帮助，并且可以自己上下床或椅子。您也应该基本能自己上厕所。 您需要特别小心，避免人工髋关节脱位，尤其是在手术后的头几个月。您需要学习一些锻炼来增强新髋关节的力量，并采取一些特别的预防措施。 出院回家后 1 到 2 周内，家里需要有人陪伴您。您需要他人帮助准备饭菜、洗澡、在家中走动以及完成其他日常活动。 随着时间推移，您应该可以逐渐恢复到以前的活动水平。但您需要避免某些运动，比如高山滑雪或橄榄球、足球等对抗性运动。不过，您应该可以进行一些低冲击活动，比如徒步、园艺、游泳、打网球和打高尔夫。 家庭环境布置 您的床高度应当适中：当您坐在床边时，双脚能着地；同时，床又要足够高，以便您坐在床边时，髋关节高于膝关节。您不一定需要医院用床，但床垫应当较硬、较结实。 清除家中的绊倒危险。 学习如何预防跌倒。把从一个房间走到另一个房间路径上的松散电线或电源线移走。移走松散的小地毯。不要在家里养小型宠物。修补门口不平整的地面。使用良好的照明。 让浴室更安全。在浴缸或淋浴间以及马桶旁安装扶手。在浴缸或淋浴间放置防滑垫。 走路时不要手里拿东西。您可能需要用双手来帮助保持平衡。您可以在助行器或拐杖上挂一个口袋或收纳袋来装东西。 把常用物品放在容易拿到的地方。 在厨房、卧室、浴室以及您经常使用的其他房间里放一把靠背结实的椅子。这样，您在做日常事情时可以坐着完成。 尽量把家里布置成不需要上下楼梯的样子。一些建议包括： 在一楼摆放一张床，或者使用一楼的卧室。 在您白天大部分时间所在的楼层设置一个卫生间，或者放置一个便携式坐便椅。 活动 在走路、坐下、躺下、穿衣、洗澡或淋浴以及进行其他活动时，您都需要小心，避免新髋关节脱位。避免坐在太低的椅子或软沙发上。 回家后要保持活动和行走。尽量不要一次坐超过 45 分钟。如果需要坐更久，45 分钟后要起来活动一下。 在外科医生允许之前，不要把全身重量压在做了手术的那一侧髋关节上。先从短时间的活动开始，然后逐渐延长活动时间。您的外科医生或物理治疗师会给您安排在家做的锻炼。 在您需要的时候，继续使用拐杖或助行器。停止使用前请先咨询您的外科医生。 几天后，您可能可以做一些简单的家务。但不要做较重的家务，比如吸尘或洗衣服。要记住，一开始您会很容易感到疲劳。不要下蹲去打扫卫生。 您可以系一个小腰包或背一个小背包，或者在助行器上挂一个篮子或结实的袋子，这样就可以随身带着一些小物品，比如手机和记事本。 伤口护理 保持伤口上的敷料（绷带）清洁、干燥。您可以按照外科医生告诉您的时间更换敷料。如果敷料变脏或弄湿了，一定要及时更换。更换敷料时请按以下步骤进行： 用肥皂和清水把双手彻底洗干净。 小心地取下敷料。不要用力猛拉。如果需要，可以用无菌水或生理盐水浸湿部分敷料，帮助将其松开。 用生理盐水浸湿干净的纱布，从切口的一端向另一端擦拭。不要在同一部位来回擦。 用干净、干燥的纱布以同样的方式擦干切口。只沿一个方向擦或轻轻拍干。 检查伤口是否有感染迹象。这些包括明显肿胀和发红，以及有异味的渗出物。 按照之前教您的方法重新敷上新的敷料。 缝线（针线）或皮肤钉一般在手术后大约 10 到 14 天拆除。手术后 3 到 4 天内，或者在外科医生允许之前，不要洗淋浴。可以洗淋浴时，让水从切口上方流过，但不要用力搓洗切口，也不要让水直接冲击切口。不要泡澡，不要泡热水浴池，也不要去游泳池泡水。 伤口周围可能会有淤青。这是正常现象，会自行消退。切口周围的皮肤可能会有些发红，这也是正常的。 自我护理 您的外科医生会给您开止痛药处方。回家后请尽快去配药，以便需要时可以马上服用。当您开始感觉疼痛时就服用止痛药。不要等太久再吃药，否则疼痛可能会比应有的程度更严重。 在康复早期，在增加活动量或做物理治疗前大约 30 分钟服用止痛药，可以帮助控制疼痛。 医生可能会让您穿戴专用的弹力袜（压力袜）大约 6 周。这有助于预防血栓形成。您可能还需要服用抗凝药（血液稀释药）2 到 4 周，以降低血栓风险。所有药物都要严格按照外科医生的指示服用。这也有助于淤青更快消退。 您的外科医生会告诉您何时可以恢复性生活。 有假体（如人工关节）的人，需要特别注意预防感染。以前...

Hip Replacement Surgery - Discharge Instructions You had surgery to replace part or all of your hip joint with an artificial joint (called a prosthesis). This article tells you how to care for your new hip after discharge. During Hospitalization You had hip replacement surgery to replace part or all of your hip joint with an artificial joint. This artificial joint is called a prosthesis. What to Know After Discharge When you are discharged, you should be able to walk using a walker or crutches without needing much help. Most people no longer need them after 2 to 4 weeks. Ask your surgeon when you can stop using crutches. You should also be able to dress yourself with a small amount of help, and be able to get in and out of bed or a chair by yourself. You should also be able to use the toilet without needing much help. You need to be careful not to dislocate your artificial hip, especially in the first few months after surgery. You need to learn exercises to make your new hip stronger and take special precautions. After discharge or leaving the rehabilitation center, you will need someone to stay with you at home for 1 to 2 weeks. You will need someone to help prepare meals, bathe, move around the room, and do other daily activities. Over time, you should be able to return to your previous activity level. You will need to avoid some sports, such as alpine skiing or contact sports like football and soccer. But you should be able to do low-impact activities like hiking, gardening, swimming, playing tennis, and playing golf. Home Setup Your bed should be low enough that when you sit on the edge of the bed, your feet can touch the ground. Your bed should also be high enough that when you sit on the edge of the bed, your hips are higher than your knees. You may not need a medical bed, but the mattress should be firm. Remove tripping hazards from your home. Learn to prevent falls. Remove loose wires or cables from areas you pass through when walking from one room...

Original English:

Heart Failure - Discharge Heart failure is a condition in which the heart is no longer able to pump oxygen-rich blood to the rest of the body efficiently. When symptoms become severe, a hospital stay may be necessary. This article discusses what you need to do to take care of yourself when you leave the hospital. When You're in the Hospital You were in the hospital to have your heart failure treated. Heart failure occurs when the muscles of your heart are weak or have trouble relaxing, or both. Your heart is a pump that moves fluids through your body. As with any pump, if the flow out of the pump is not enough, fluids do not move well and they get stuck in places they should not be. In your body, this means that fluid collects in your lungs, abdomen, and legs. While you were in the hospital: Your health care team closely adjusted the fluids you drank or received through an intravenous (IV) line. They also watched and measured how much urine you produced. You may have received medicines to help your body get rid of extra fluids. You may have had tests to check how well your heart was working. What to Expect at Home Your energy will slowly return. You may need help taking care of yourself when you first get home. You may feel sad or depressed. All of these things are normal. Checking Yourself at Home Weigh yourself every morning on the same scale when you get up -- before you eat but after you use the bathroom. Make sure you are wearing similar clothing each time you weigh yourself. Write down your weight every day on a chart so that you can keep track of it. Throughout the day, ask yourself: Is my energy level normal? Do I get more short of breath when I am doing my everyday activities? Are my clothes or shoes feeling tight? Are my ankles or legs swelling? Am I coughing more often? Does my cough sound wet? Do I get short of breath at night or when I lie down? 心力衰竭 - 出院 心力衰竭是指心脏无法有效地将富含氧气的血液泵送到身体其他部位的一种疾病。当症状变得严重时，可能需要住院。本文讨论您出院后需要如何照顾自己。 住院期间 您住院是为了治疗心力衰竭。心力衰竭发生在您的心肌变弱或难以放松时，或两者同时发生。 您的心脏是一个将液体输送到全身的泵。就像任何泵一样，如果泵出的流量不足，液体就无法正常流动，并会滞留在不该滞留的地方。在您的身体里，这意味着液体会积聚在肺部、腹部和腿部。 住院期间： * 您的医疗团队密切调整了您通过口服或静脉输液（IV）摄入的液体量。他们还观察并测量了您的尿量。 * 您可能接受了帮助身体排出多余液体的药物。 * 您可能接受了检查心脏功能状况的测试。 出院后会发生什么 您的精力会慢慢恢复。刚回家时，您可能需要他人帮助照顾自己。您可能会感到悲伤或抑郁。这些都是正常的。 在家自我监测 每天早上起床后、进食前、但上完厕所后，用同一个秤称体重。确保每次称重时穿着相似的衣物。每天将体重记录在图表上，以便跟踪。 在一天中，问问自己： * 我的精力水平正常吗？ * 我在进行日常活动时是否更容易气短？ * 我的衣服或鞋子是否感觉紧绷？ * 我的脚踝或腿部是否肿胀？ * 我是否咳嗽更频繁？咳嗽声音是否湿咳？ * 我在夜间或躺下时是否气短？ 如果您出现新的（或不同的）症状，问问自己： * 我是否吃了与平时不同的食物或尝试了新食物？ * 我是否按时按量服用了所有药物？ 饮食与液体摄入 您的医疗服务提供者可能会要求您限制饮水量。 * 当您的病情不太严重时，可能不需要过多限制液体摄入。 * 随着心力衰竭加重，您可能需要将液体摄入量限制在每天6到9杯（1.5到2升）。 您需要减少盐的摄入量。盐会让您感到口渴，而口渴会导致您饮用过多液体。多余的盐还会使液体滞留在体内。许多尝起来不咸或您没有额外加盐的食物仍然含有大量盐分。 您可能需要服用利尿剂（去水丸）。 不要饮酒。酒精会使您的心肌更难正常工作。在特殊场合，如果会提供酒精和您需要避免的食物，请咨询您的提供者该如何处理。 如果您吸烟，请戒烟。如果需要帮助，请寻求帮助。不要让任何人在您家中吸烟。 了解更多关于您应该吃什么来使心脏和血管更健康的信息。 * 避免高脂肪食物。 * 远离快餐店。 * 避免某些预制食品和冷冻食品。 尽量避免让您感到压力的事情。如果您一直感到压力，或非常悲伤，请与您的提供者交谈，他们可以为您转介咨询师。 服用心脏药物 在回家前配齐所有处方药物。严格按照提供者告知的方式服药非常重要。在没有先咨询提供者的情况下，不要服用任何其他药物或草药。 用水服药。不要用葡萄柚汁服药，因为它可能会改变您身体吸收某些药物的方式。请咨询您的提供者或药剂师这是否会对您造成影响。 以下药物通常会开给许多心力衰竭患者。但有时可能存在不适合服用的原因。这些药物可能有助于保护您的心脏。如果您尚未服用以下任何药物，请与您的提供者讨论： * 抗血小板药物（血液稀释剂），如阿司匹林或氯吡格雷（波立维），有助于防止血液凝固 * 抗凝药物（血液稀释剂），如华法林（香豆素），有助于防止血液凝固 * β受体阻滞剂和ACE抑制剂药物，以及其他用于降低血压和治疗心肌的药物 * 他汀类药物或其他降低胆固醇的药物 在改变服药方式之前，请咨询您的提供者。切勿擅自停用这些心脏药物，或您可能正在服用的糖尿病、高血压或其他疾病的任何药物。 如果您正在服用血液稀释剂，如华法林（香豆素），您需要接受额外的血液检查以确保剂量正确。某些其他血液稀释剂则不需要这样做。 活动 您的提供者可能会将您转介到心脏康复计划。在那里，您将学习如何逐步增加运动量以及如何照顾您的心脏病。请确保避免提重物。 请确保您了解心力衰竭和心脏病发作的警示信号。了解当您出现胸痛或心绞痛时该如何处理。 在重新开始性活动前，请务必咨询您的提供者。在未事先咨询的情况下，不要服用西地那非（万艾可）、伐地那非（艾力达）、他达拉非（希爱力）或任何治疗勃起问题的草药。 请确保您的家布置得安全且便于您活动，以避免跌倒。 如果您无法多走动，请向您的提供者咨询一些您可以在坐着时进行的锻炼。 随访 请确保按照提供者建议的时间表接种流感疫苗和COVID-19疫苗（通常每年一次）。您可能还需要接种肺炎球菌疫苗（肺炎疫苗）。请咨询您的提供者。 您的提供者可能会打电话给您，了解您的状况，并确保您在监测体重和服药。 您需要在提供者的诊所进行随访预约。 您可能需要接受某些实验室检查，以检查钠和钾水平，并监测肾脏功能。 何时致电医生 如果出现以下情况，请联系您的提供者： * 一天内体重增加超过2磅（1公斤），或一周内增加超过5磅（2公斤）。 * 您感到非常疲倦和虚弱。 * 您感到头...

Heart Failure - Discharge Heart failure is a disease where the heart cannot effectively pump oxygen-rich blood to other parts of the body. When symptoms become severe, hospitalization may be needed. This article discusses how you need to take care of yourself after discharge. During Hospitalization You were hospitalized to treat heart failure. Heart failure occurs when your heart muscle becomes weak or has difficulty relaxing, or both occur simultaneously. Your heart is a pump that transports liquid throughout the body. Just like any pump, if the pumped flow is insufficient, liquid cannot flow normally and will stagnate in places it shouldn't. In your body, this means liquid will accumulate in the lungs, abdomen, and legs. During hospitalization: * Your medical team closely adjusted the amount of liquid you took in through oral intake or intravenous infusion (IV). They also observed and measured your urine output. * You may have received medications that help the body expel excess liquid. * You may have received tests that examine the condition of heart function. What Happens After Discharge Your energy will slowly recover. When you first return home, you may need others to help take care of you. You may feel sad or depressed. These are all normal. Home Self-Monitoring Every morning after getting up, before eating, but after using the toilet, weigh yourself with the same scale. Ensure you wear similar clothing each time you weigh. Record your weight on a chart daily to track. During the day, ask yourself: * Is my energy level normal? * Do I get short of breath more easily when performing daily activities? * Do my clothes or shoes feel tight? * Are my ankles or legs swollen? * Am I coughing more frequently? Does the cough sound wet? * Am I short of breath at night or when lying down? If you have new (or different) symptoms, ask yourself: * Did I eat different foods than usual or try new foods? * Did I take all medications on time and in the correct amount?...

Original English:

Taking warfarin Warfarin is a medicine that makes your blood less likely to form clots. It is important that you take warfarin exactly as you have been told. Changing how you take your warfarin, taking other medicines with it or at different times, and eating certain foods can change the way warfarin works in your body. If this happens, you may be more likely to form a clot or have bleeding problems. What to Expect at Home Warfarin is a medicine that makes your blood less likely to form clots. This may be important if: You have already had blood clots in your leg, arm, heart, or brain. Your health care provider is worried that a blood clot may form in your body. People who have a new heart valve, a large heart, a heart rhythm that is not normal, or other heart problems may need to take warfarin. When you are taking warfarin, you may be more likely to bleed, even from activities you have always done. Changing how you take your warfarin, taking other medicines, and eating certain foods all can change the way warfarin works in your body. If this happens, you may be more likely to form a clot or have bleeding problems. Taking Warfarin It is important that you take warfarin exactly as you have been told. Take only the dose your provider has prescribed. If you miss a dose, contact your provider for advice. If your pills look different from your last prescription, contact your provider or pharmacist right away. The tablets are different colors, depending on the dose. The dose is also marked on the pill. Your provider will test your blood at regular visits. This is called an INR test or sometimes a PT test. The test helps make sure you are taking the right amount of warfarin to help your body. Alcohol and some medicines can change how warfarin works in your body. DO NOT drink alcohol while you are taking warfarin. Original English:

Heart attack – discharge A heart attack occurs when blood flow to a part of your heart is blocked long enough that part of the heart muscle is damaged or dies. This article discusses what you need to do to take care of yourself after you leave the hospital. When You're in the Hospital You were in the hospital because you had a heart attack. A heart attack occurs when blood flow to a part of your heart is blocked long enough that part of the heart muscle is damaged or dies. What to Expect at Home You may feel sad. You may feel anxious and as though you have to be very careful about what you do. All of these feelings are normal. They go away for most people after 2 or 3 weeks. You may also feel tired when you leave the hospital to go home. Activity You should know the signs and symptoms of angina. You may feel pressure, squeezing, burning, or tightness in your chest. You may also notice these symptoms in your arms, shoulders, neck, jaw, throat, or back. Some people also feel discomfort in their back, shoulders, and stomach area. You may have indigestion or feel sick to your stomach. You may feel tired and be short of breath, sweaty, lightheaded, or weak. You may have angina during physical activity, such as climbing stairs or walking uphill, lifting, sexual activity, or when you are out in cold weather. It can also happen when you are resting or it can wake you up when you are sleeping. Know how to treat your chest pain when it happens. Talk with your health care provider about what to do. Take it easy for the first 4 to 6 weeks after your heart attack. Avoid heavy lifting. Get some help with household chores if you can. Take 30 to 60 minutes to rest in the afternoon for first 4 to 6 weeks. Try to go to bed early and get plenty of sleep. Before starting to exercise, your provider may have you do an exercise test and recommend an exercise plan. This may happen before you leave the hospital or soon afterward. Original English:

High blood pressure - what to ask your doctor When your heart pumps blood into your arteries, the pressure of the blood against the artery walls is called your blood pressure. Your blood pressure is given as two numbers: systolic over diastolic blood pressure. Your systolic blood pressure is the highest blood pressure during the course of your heart beat cycle. Your diastolic blood pressure is the lowest pressure. When your blood pressure gets too high, it puts extra stress on your heart and blood vessels. If your blood pressure stays high all the time, you will be at a higher risk for heart attacks and other vascular (blood vessel) diseases, strokes, kidney disease, and other health problems. Below are questions you may want to ask your health care provider to help you take care of your blood pressure. Questions How can I change the way I live to lower my blood pressure? Are there other spices that I can use to make my food taste good? Is it OK to drink alcohol? How much is OK? What can I do to stop smoking? Is it OK to be around other people who are smoking? Should I check my blood pressure at home? What type of equipment should I buy? Where can I learn how to use it? How often do I need to check my blood pressure? Should I write it down and bring it to my next visit? If I cannot check my own blood pressure, where else can I have it checked? What should my blood pressure reading be? Should I rest before taking my blood pressure? When should I contact my provider? What is my cholesterol? Do I need to take medicines for it? Is it OK to be sexually active? Item: EVAL_0330 | Document: DIAB_002 | Model: Model D

Original English:

Low blood sugar - self-care Low blood sugar is a condition that occurs when your blood sugar (glucose) is lower than normal. Low blood sugar may occur in people with diabetes who are taking insulin or certain other medicines to control their diabetes. Low blood sugar can cause dangerous symptoms. Learn how to recognize the symptoms of low blood sugar and how to prevent them. What is Low Blood Sugar? Low blood sugar is called hypoglycemia. A blood sugar level below 70 mg/dL (3.9 mmol/L) is low and can harm you. A blood sugar level below 54 mg/dL (3.0 mmol/L) is a cause for immediate action. You are at risk for low blood sugar if you have diabetes and are taking any of the following diabetes medicines: Insulin Glyburide (Micronase), glipizide (Glucotrol), glimepiride (Amaryl), repaglinide (Prandin), or nateglinide (Starlix) You are also at increased risk of having low blood sugar if you have had previous low blood sugar levels. Recognizing Low Blood Sugar Know how to tell when your blood sugar is getting low. Symptoms include: Weakness or feeling tired Shaking Sweating Headache Hunger Feeling uneasy, nervous, or anxious Feeling cranky Trouble thinking clearly Double or blurry vision Fast or pounding heartbeat Sometimes your blood sugar may be too low even if you do not have symptoms. If it gets too low, you may: Faint Have a seizure Go into a coma Some people who have had diabetes for a long time stop being able to sense low blood sugar. This is called hypoglycemic unawareness. Ask your health care provider if wearing a continuous glucose monitor and sensor can help you detect when your blood sugar is getting too low in order to help prevent symptoms. Check Your Blood Sugar Often Talk with your provider about when you should check your blood sugar every day. People who have low blood sugar need to check their blood sugar more often. 低血糖 - 自我护理 低血糖是指血糖（葡萄糖）低于正常水平的一种状况。低血糖可能发生在使用胰岛素或某些其他药物来控制糖尿病的患者身上。低血糖可能引起危险的症状。请学习如何识别低血糖的症状以及如何预防。 什么是低血糖？ 低血糖称为低血糖症。血糖水平低于70 mg/dL（3.9 mmol/L）属于低血糖，可能会对您造成伤害。血糖水平低于54 mg/dL（3.0 mmol/L）需要立即采取行动。 如果您患有糖尿病并且正在使用以下任何一种糖尿病药物，您就有发生低血糖的风险： - 胰岛素 - 格列本脲（Micronase）、格列吡嗪（Glucotrol）、格列美脲（Amaryl）、瑞格列奈（Prandin）或那格列奈（Starlix） 如果您以前出现过低血糖，您发生低血糖的风险也会增加。 识别低血糖 要知道如何判断您的血糖正在降低。症状包括： - 虚弱或感觉疲倦 - 颤抖 - 出汗 - 头痛 - 饥饿 - 感觉不安、紧张或焦虑 - 感觉烦躁 - 思维不清 - 复视或视力模糊 - 心跳过快或剧烈 有时即使您没有症状，您的血糖也可能过低。如果血糖过低，您可能会： - 昏厥 - 癫痫发作 - 陷入昏迷 一些长期患有糖尿病的人无法再感知低血糖。这称为低血糖无意识。请咨询您的医疗保健提供者，佩戴连续血糖监测仪和传感器是否可以帮助您检测血糖何时过低，从而帮助预防症状。 经常检查您的血糖 与您的提供者讨论您每天应该在什么时间检查血糖。有低血糖的人需要更频繁地检查血糖。 低血糖最常见的原因包括： - 在错误的时间使用胰岛素或糖尿病药物 - 使用过多的胰岛素或糖尿病药物 - 使用胰岛素来纠正高血糖但没有进食任何食物 - 在使用胰岛素或糖尿病药物后，正餐或零食吃得不够 - 漏餐（这可能意味着您的长效胰岛素剂量过高，因此您应该与您的提供者讨论） - 在使用药物后等待太久才进食 - 运动量过大或在您不常运动的时间运动 - 在运动前没有检查血糖或没有调整胰岛素剂量 - 饮酒 预防低血糖 预防低血糖比治疗低血糖更好。随时携带速效糖源。 当您运动时，请检查您的血糖水平。确保随身携带零食。 与您的提供者讨论在运动当天减少胰岛素剂量。 咨询您的提供者是否需要睡前零食来预防夜间低血糖。蛋白质零食可能是最佳选择。 不要在空腹时饮酒。女性每天饮酒应限制在1杯以内，男性每天应限制在2杯以内。 家人和朋友应该知道如何提供帮助。他们应该知道： - 低血糖的症状以及如何判断您是否有这些症状。 - 他们应该给您多少食物以及什么种类的食物。 - 何时呼叫紧急救援。 - 如何注射胰高血糖素，一种能提高血糖的激素。您的提供者会告诉您何时使用这种药物。 如果您患有糖尿病，请始终佩戴医疗警示手环或项链。这有助于急救医务人员知道您患有糖尿病。 当您的血糖降低时 每当您出现低血糖症状时，请检查您的血糖。如果您的血糖低于70 mg/dL，请立即进行自我治疗。 1. 食用含有约15克（g）碳水化合物的食物。例如： - 4片葡萄糖片 - 半杯（4盎司或120 mL）果汁或普通非无糖汽水 - 5到6块硬糖 - 1汤匙（tbsp）或15 mL糖，纯糖或溶于水中 - 1汤匙（15 mL）蜂蜜或糖浆 2. 在进食任何其他食物前等待约15分钟。注意不要吃得太多。这可能导致高血糖和体重增加。 3. 再次检查您的血糖。 4. 如果15分钟后您没有感觉好转，且血糖仍低于70 mg/dL（3.9 mmol/L），请再食用一份含15克碳水化合物的零食。 如果您的血糖处于较安全的范围——高于70 mg/dL（3.9 mmol/L）——且距离下一餐还有一个多小时，您可能需要食用一份含碳水化合物和蛋白质的零食。 请咨询您的提供者如何处理这种情况。如果这些提高血糖的步骤无效，请立即联系您的提供者。 咨询您的医生或护士 如果您使用胰岛素且血糖经常或持续偏低，请咨询您的提供者或护士您是否： - 胰岛素注射方式是否正确 - 需要不同类型的针头 - 应该改变胰岛素的用量 - 应该改变胰岛素的种类 在未与您的提供者或护士交谈之前，不要做任何更改。 有时低血糖可能是由于误服了错误的药物。请与您的药剂师核对您的药物。 何时呼叫医生 如果在食用含糖零食后低血糖症状没有改善，请让他人开车送您去急诊室或拨打911或当地急救电话。当您的血糖偏低时，请勿开车。 如果低血糖患者神志不清或无法唤醒，请立即寻求医疗帮助，因为这是医疗紧急情况。

Back-Translation (to English):

Hypoglycemia - Self-care Hypoglycemia refers to a condition where blood sugar (glucose) is below normal levels. Hypoglycemia can occur in patients using insulin or certain other medications to control diabetes. Hypoglycemia can cause dangerous symptoms. Please learn how to recognize the symptoms of hypoglycemia and how to prevent it. What is hypoglycemia? Hypoglycemia is called hypoglycemia. Blood sugar levels below 70 mg/dL (3.9 mmol/L) are considered hypoglycemia and may cause harm to you. Blood sugar levels below 54 mg/dL (3.0 mmol/L) require immediate action. If you have diabetes and are using any of the following diabetes medications, you have a risk of developing hypoglycemia: - Insulin - Glyburide (Micronase), Glipizide (Glucotrol), Glimepiride (Amaryl), Repaglinide (Prandin) or Nateglinide (Starlix) If you have had hypoglycemia before, your risk of developing hypoglycemia also increases. Recognizing Hypoglycemia You need to know how to tell if your blood sugar is dropping. Symptoms include: - Weakness or feeling tired - Trembling - Sweating - Headache - Hunger - Feeling restless, nervous, or anxious - Feeling irritable - Unclear thinking - Double vision or blurred vision - Fast or pounding heartbeat Sometimes even if you have no symptoms, your blood sugar may be too low. If blood sugar is too low, you may: - Faint - Seizures - Fall into a coma Some people with long-term diabetes can no longer sense hypoglycemia. This is called hypoglycemia unawareness. Please consult your healthcare provider whether wearing a continuous glucose monitor and sensor can help you detect when your blood sugar is too low, thereby helping to prevent symptoms. Check Your Blood Sugar Frequently Discuss with your provider what times of day you should check your blood sugar. People with hypoglycemia need to check their blood sugar more frequently. The most common causes of hypoglycemia include: - Using insulin or diabetes medication at the wrong time - Using too much insul...

Item: EVAL_0337 | Document: RESP_001 | Model: Model D

Original English:

Asthma - quick-relief drugs Asthma quick-relief medicines work fast to control asthma symptoms. You take them when you are coughing, wheezing, having trouble breathing, or having an asthma attack. They are also called rescue medicines. Many of these medicines are called "bronchodilators" because they open (dilate) and help relax the muscles of your airways (bronchi). You and your health care provider can make a plan for the quick-relief medicines that work for you. This plan will include when you should take them and how much you should take. Plan ahead. Make sure you do not run out. Bring enough medicine with you when you travel. Short-acting Beta-agonists Short-acting beta-agonists are the most common quick-relief medicines for treating asthma attacks and are considered to be bronchodilators. They can be used just before exercising to help prevent asthma symptoms caused by exercise. They work by relaxing the muscles of your airways, and this lets you breathe better during an attack. Tell your provider if you are using quick-relief medicines twice a week or more to control your asthma symptoms. Your asthma may not be under control, and your provider may need to change your dose of daily control medicines. Some quick-relief asthma medicines include: Albuterol (ProAir HFA, Proventil HFA, Ventolin HFA) Levalbuterol (Xopenex HFA) Metaproterenol Terbutaline Short-acting beta-agonists may cause these side effects: Anxiety. Fast and irregular heartbeats. Call your provider right away if you have this side effect. Headache. Restlessness. Tremor (your hand or another part of your body may shake). Oral Steroids Your provider might prescribe oral steroids when you have an asthma attack that is not going away. These are medicines that you take by mouth as pills, capsules, or liquids. Oral steroids are not quick-relief medicines but are often given for 7 to 14 days when your symptoms flare-up. Oral steroids include: Methylprednisolone Prednisone Prednisolone

COPD - what to ask your doctor Chronic obstructive pulmonary disease (COPD) damages your lungs. This can make it hard for you to get enough oxygen and clear carbon dioxide from your lungs. For what side effects should I contact my provider? Am I using my inhaler the right way? Should I be using a spacer? How will I know when my inhalers are getting empty? Item: EVAL_0354 | Document: MED_001 | Model: Model D

Original English:

ACE inhibitors Angiotensin-converting enzyme (ACE) inhibitors are medicines. They treat heart, blood vessel, and kidney problems. How ACE inhibitors help ACE inhibitors are used to treat heart disease and high blood pressure. These medicines make your heart work less hard by lowering your blood pressure. This keeps some kinds of heart disease from getting worse. Most people who have heart failure take one of these medicines or similar medicines. These medicines treat high blood pressure, strokes, or heart attacks. They may help lower your risk for stroke or heart attack. They are also used to treat kidney problems. This can help keep your kidneys from getting worse or even improve the function of your kidneys, especially if you have diabetes. If you have these problems, ask your health care provider if you should be taking these medicines. Types of ACE inhibitors There are many different names and brands of ACE inhibitors. Most work as well as another. Side effects may be different for different ones. Taking Your ACE inhibitors ACE inhibitors are pills that you take by mouth. Take all of your medicines as your provider told you to. Follow up with your provider regularly. Your provider will check your blood pressure and do blood tests to make sure the medicines are working properly. Your provider may change your dose from time to time. In addition: Try to take your medicines at the same time each day. Don't stop taking your medicines without talking to your provider first. Plan ahead so that you do not run out of medicine. Make sure you have enough with you when you travel. Before taking ibuprofen (Advil, Motrin) or aspirin, talk to your provider. Tell your provider what other medicines you are taking, including anything you bought without a prescription, diuretics (water pills), potassium pills, or herbal or dietary supplements. Stroke - discharge You were in the hospital after having a stroke. A stroke happens when blood flow to part of the brain stops. At home follow your health care provider's instructions on self-care. You may have physical or occupational therapy to restore your ability to perform these functions. Depression after a stroke is fairly common as you learn to live with the changes. It may develop soon after the stroke or up to 2 years after the stroke. Do not drive your car without your provider's permission. Original English:

Surgical wound care - open An incision is a cut through the skin that is made during surgery. It is also called a surgical wound. Some incisions are small, others are long. The size of the incision depends on the kind of surgery you had. Sometimes, an incision breaks open. This may happen along the entire cut or just part of it. Your surgeon may decide not to close it again with sutures (stitches). What to Expect at Home If your surgeon does not close your wound again with sutures, you need to care for it at home, since it may take time to heal. The wound will heal from the bottom to the top. A dressing helps absorb drainage and keep the skin from closing before the wound underneath fills in. Proper Handwashing It is important to clean your hands before you change your dressing. You can use an alcohol-based cleanser. Or, you can wash your hands using these steps: Take all jewelry off your hands. Wet your hands, pointing them downward under warm running water. Add soap and wash your hands for 15 to 30 seconds (sing "Happy Birthday" or the "Alphabet Song" one time through). Clean under your nails also. Rinse well. Dry with a clean towel. Removing the Old Dressing Your health care provider will tell you how often to change your dressing. To prepare for the dressing change: Clean your hands before touching the dressing. Make sure you have all the supplies handy. Have a clean work surface. Remove the old dressing: Carefully loosen the tape from your skin. Use a clean (not sterile) medical glove to grab the old dressing and pull it off. If the dressing sticks to the wound, wet it and try again, unless your provider instructed you to pull it off dry. Put the old dressing in a plastic bag and set it aside. Clean your hands again after you take off the old dressing. --- 开放性手术伤口护理 切口是手术过程中在皮肤上切开的口子，也称为手术伤口。有些切口很小，有些则较长。切口的大小取决于您接受的手术类型。 有时切口会裂开。这可能发生在整个切口或仅部分切口上。您的外科医生可能会决定不再用缝线（缝合）将其重新闭合。 居家护理须知 如果您的外科医生没有用缝线重新闭合伤口，您需要在家中进行护理，因为伤口愈合可能需要一段时间。伤口将从底部到顶部愈合。敷料有助于吸收渗出液，并防止皮肤表面在伤口底部愈合前过早闭合。 正确洗手 在更换敷料前清洁双手很重要。您可以使用含酒精的洗手液。或者，您可以按照以下步骤洗手： 1. 取下手上的所有首饰。 2. 将双手朝下放在温水流下冲洗。 3. 涂抹肥皂，洗手15至30秒（唱一遍《生日快乐歌》或《字母歌》）。也要清洁指甲下方。 4. 彻底冲洗干净。 5. 用干净的毛巾擦干。 移除旧敷料 医护人员会告诉您多久更换一次敷料。为更换敷料做准备： 1. 在接触敷料前清洁双手。 2. 确保所有用品都在手边。 3. 准备一个干净的工作台面。 移除旧敷料： 1. 小心地从皮肤上揭下胶带。 2. 用一只清洁的（非无菌的）医用手套抓住旧敷料并将其取下。 3. 如果敷料粘在伤口上，请将其弄湿后再试，除非您的医护人员指示您直接将其揭下。 4. 将旧敷料放入塑料袋中并放在一旁。 5. 取下旧敷料后再次清洁双手。 护理伤口 您可以使用纱布垫或软布清洁伤口周围的皮肤： • 使用生理盐水（盐水溶液）或温和的肥皂水。 • 将纱布或布浸入生理盐水或肥皂水中，用其轻轻擦拭皮肤。 • 尽量清除所有渗出液以及可能积聚在皮肤上的干血或其他物质。 • 请勿使用皮肤清洁剂、酒精、双氧水、碘酒或含抗菌化学物质的肥皂。这些物质会损伤伤口组织并延缓愈合。 医护人员可能还要求您冲洗伤口： • 用注射器抽取盐水或肥皂水，以医护人员建议的为准。 • 将注射器放置在距离伤口1至6英寸（2.5至15厘米）的位置。用力喷射以冲走伤口内的渗出液和分泌物。 • 用一块干净、柔软、干燥的布或纱布轻轻拍干伤口。 • 除非医护人员同意，否则请勿在伤口上或周围涂抹任何乳液、乳霜或草药制剂。 更换新敷料 按照医护人员教您的方法将清洁的敷料敷在伤口上。您可能正在使用需要在敷用前弄湿的湿干敷料。 完成后清洁双手。 将旧敷料和其他使用过的用品丢弃在防水塑料袋中。将其密封严实，然后再套一个袋子，再放入垃圾桶。 将更换敷料时弄脏的衣物与其他衣物分开洗涤。询问医护人员是否需要在洗涤水中添加漂白剂。 敷料只能使用一次。切勿重复使用。 何时致电医生 如果出现以下情况，请联系医护人员： • 伤口部位出现更多发红、疼痛、肿胀或出血。 • 伤口变大或变深，或看起来干燥或发黑。 • 伤口渗出液增多或变得浓稠、呈棕褐色、绿色或黄色，或有异味（这表明有脓液）。 • 您的体温达到100.5°F（38°C）或更高。 ---

This article tells you what you need to do to care for your new hip when you leave the hospital. When You're in the Hospital You had a hip joint replacement surgery to replace all or part of your hip joint with an artificial joint. This artificial joint is called a prosthesis. What to Expect at Home By the time you go home, you should be able to walk with a walker or crutches without needing much help. Most people do not need them after 2 to 4 weeks. Check with your surgeon about when to stop using crutches. You should also be able to dress yourself with only a little help and be able to get into and out of your bed or a chair by yourself. You should also be able to use the toilet without much help. You will need to be careful that you do not dislocate your artificial hip, especially in the first few months after surgery. You will need to learn exercises that make your new hip stronger and take special precautions. You will need to have someone with you at home for 1 to 2 weeks after you leave the hospital or rehab center. You will need help preparing meals, bathing, moving around the house, and doing other daily activities. Over time, you should be able to return to your former level of activity. You will need to avoid some sports, such as downhill skiing or contact sports like football and soccer. But you should be able to do low impact activities, such as hiking, gardening, swimming, playing tennis, and golfing. Home Setup Your bed should be low enough for your feet to touch the floor when you sit on the edge of the bed. Your bed should also be high enough so that your hips are higher than your knees when you sit on the edge. You may not need a hospital bed, but your mattress should be firm. Keep tripping hazards out of your home. Learn to prevent falls. Remove loose wires or cords from areas you walk through to get from one...

Translation (Chinese (Simplified)):

髋关节置换术 - 出院 您接受了手术，用人工关节（称为假体）置换全部或部分髋关节。本文告诉您出院后如何护理您的新髋关节。 住院期间 您接受了髋关节置换手术，用人工关节置换全部或部分髋关节。这个人工关节称为假体。 出院后预期情况 到您出院时，您应该能够借助助行器或拐杖行走，而不需要太多帮助。大多数人在2到4周后不再需要它们。请向您的外科医生咨询何时停止使用拐杖。 您还应该能够在只有少量帮助的情况下自己穿衣，并且能够自己上下床或椅子。您还应该能够在不需要太多帮助的情况下使用厕所。 您需要小心不要使人工髋关节脱位，尤其是在手术后的最初几个月内。您需要学习锻炼来增强新髋关节的力量，并采取特殊预防措施。 出院后或离开康复中心后，您需要有人在家中陪伴1到2周。您需要帮助准备饭菜、洗澡、在屋内走动以及进行其他日常活动。 随着时间的推移，您应该能够恢复到以前的活动水平。您需要避免某些运动，例如下坡滑雪或接触性运动，如橄榄球和足球。但您应该能够进行低冲击活动，例如徒步、园艺、游泳、打网球和高尔夫球。 居家布置 您的床应该足够低，使您坐在床沿时双脚能够触地。您的床也应该足够高，使您坐在床沿时臀部高于膝盖。您可能不需要医院病床，但您的床垫应该坚硬。 清除家中的绊倒隐患。 学会预防跌倒。 • 从您穿行于房间之间的区域移除松散的电线或绳索。 • 移除松散的小地毯。 • 不要在家中饲养小型宠物。 • 修复门口任何不平整的地板。 • 使用良好的照明。 让浴室更安全。 • 在浴缸或淋浴间以及马桶旁安装扶手。 • 在浴缸或淋浴间放置防滑垫。 走动时不要携带任何东西。您可能需要双手来帮助保持平衡。您可以在助行器或拐杖上安装口袋或支架来放置物品。 将物品放在容易拿到的地方。 在厨房、卧室、浴室和其他您会使用的房间放置一把靠背坚固的椅子。这样，您在做日常事务时可以坐下。 布置您的家，使您无需上下楼梯。一些建议是： 1. 在一楼布置卧室或使用一楼的卧室。 2. 在您度过大部分时间的同一楼层设置卫生间或使用便携式坐便器。 活动 在行走、坐下、躺下、穿衣、洗澡或淋浴以及进行其他活动时，您需要小心不要使新髋关节脱位。避免坐在低矮的椅子或柔软的沙发上。 回家后保持活动和行走。尽量不要一次坐超过45分钟。如果您需要坐更长时间，请在45分钟后起身走动。 在您的外科医生告知您可以之前，不要将您的全部体重放在有新髋关节的一侧。从短时间活动开始，然后逐渐增加活动时间。您的外科医生或物理治疗师会给您在家锻炼的指导。 根据需要使用助行器或拐杖。在停止使用之前，请咨询您的外科医生。 几天后，您可能能够做一些简单的家务。不要尝试做较重的家务，例如吸尘或洗衣。请记住，您一开始会很快感到疲劳。不要蹲下清洁。 佩戴一个小腰包或背包，或在助行器上安装一个篮子或结实的袋子，这样您就可以随身携带小型家居用品，如电话和记事本。 伤口护理 保持伤口上的敷料（绷带）清洁干燥。您可以根据外科医生告知您的时间更换敷料。如果敷料变脏或湿了，请务必更换。更换敷料时，请遵循以下步骤： 1. 用肥皂和水彻底洗手。 2. 小心地移除敷料。不要用力拉扯。如果需要，用无菌水或生理盐水浸湿部分敷料以帮助松动。 3. 用生理盐水浸湿一些干净的纱布，从切口的一端擦拭到另一端。不要在同一区域来回擦拭。 4. 用干净、干燥的纱布以同样的方式擦干切口。只朝一个方向擦拭或轻拍。 5. 检查伤口是否有感染迹象。这些包括严重肿胀和发红以及有难闻气味的引流液。 6. 按照示教的方法敷上新的敷料。 缝线或钉合钉将在手术后约10到14天拆除。在手术后3到4天内不要淋浴，或在您的外科医生告知您可以淋浴时才能淋浴。当您能够淋浴时，让水从切口上流过，但不要擦洗切口或让水直接冲击切口。不要在浴缸、热水浴缸或游泳池中浸泡。 您的伤口周围可能会有瘀伤。这是正常的，会自行消退。切口周围的皮肤可能会有一点发红。这也是正常的。 自我护理 您的外科医生会给您开止痛药。您回家时就去配药，以便在需要时就有药。在开始感到疼痛时服用止痛药。等待太久才服药会使您的疼痛变得比应有的更严重。 在康复的早期阶段，在增加活动或进行物理治疗前约30分钟服用止痛药可以帮助控制疼痛。 您可能需要在大约6周内穿戴特殊的弹力袜。这些袜子有助于防止血栓形成。您可能还需要服用2到4周的抗凝药物以降低血栓风险。请按照外科医生告知的方式服用所有药物。它可以帮助瘀伤更容易消退。 您的外科医生会告知您何时可以重新开始性活动。 拥有假体（如人工关节）的人需要仔细保护自己免受感染。过去曾建议在任何牙科治疗或侵入性医疗程序前服用抗生素，但除高危患者外，该建议已更改。请务必与您的外科医生确认，并告知您的牙医或其他外科医生您接受了髋关节置换术。 何时联系医生...

Back-Translation (to English):

Hip Replacement Surgery - Discharge You underwent surgery to replace all or part of your hip joint with an artificial joint (called a prosthesis). This article tells you how to care for your new hip joint after discharge. During Hospitalization You underwent hip replacement surgery to replace all or part of your hip joint with an artificial joint. This artificial joint is called a prosthesis. Expectations After Discharge By the time you are discharged, you should be able to walk with the aid of a walker or crutches without needing too much help. Most people no longer need them after 2 to 4 weeks. Please consult your surgeon about when to stop using crutches. You should also be able to dress yourself with only a little help, and be able to get in and out of bed or a chair by yourself. You should also be able to use the toilet without needing too much help. You need to be careful not to dislocate the artificial hip joint, especially within the first few months after surgery. You need to learn exercises to strengthen the new hip joint and take special precautions. After discharge or leaving the rehabilitation center, you need someone to stay with you at home for 1 to 2 weeks. You need help preparing meals, bathing, moving around the house, and performing other daily activities. Over time, you should be able to return to your previous activity level. You need to avoid certain sports, such as downhill skiing or contact sports like rugby and soccer. But you should be able to do low-impact activities such as hiking, gardening, swimming, playing tennis, and golf. Home Setup Your bed should be low enough that your feet can touch the floor when you sit on the edge of the bed. Your bed should also be high enough that your hips are higher than your knees when you sit on the edge of the bed. You may not need a hospital bed, but your mattress should be firm.
